when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是個程式設計師 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正的確是 , 要知道 , 未來將會有多大 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙出現在1936年 , 發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器是完全理論的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這些人都來自數學觀點 , 但turing告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他把數學基金給電腦科學 , 說: 「 不管你如何製作電腦科學 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	這不重要 , 如果你電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 如今 , 電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它很小 , 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種程度上 , 有一種計算能力 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做churchurchuringsis 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你得到了這個連結 , 你說這個東西是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 電腦真的很慢 , 只有慢慢地 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了給你一個想法 , 它有多慢 , 它有記憶力 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用punch卡片 , 它用了一萬次慢慢的第一zx81 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有強烈的包裝 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	你可以加上更多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天我們來到哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	所以有計劃 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在華盛頓特區 , 科學博物館有數百個計劃和數百個計劃和數以千計的頁面 , 由查爾斯•巴布所寫的 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是我們稱之為 「 計劃28 」 的名字 , 也是我創立了 「 飛機計畫 」 的名字 , 也是我們所謂的 「 慈善計畫 」 , 創立了 「 飛機 」 的名字 , 也是我從doronsade所創立的 「 飛行器 」 的名字 , 也是 「 飛機 」 的名字 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯斯頓 , 我們會建造出分析的引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計畫有許多部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	首先是掃描的掃描 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二 , 目前正在研究所有的計畫 , 來決定要做什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬機器 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它完成時 , 你得去看這段影片 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到了cpu操作 , 我知道電腦如何運作 , 因為不是在你面前的微小晶片 , 你必須看著這件很棒的事 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到了cpu操作 , 我知道電腦如何運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在我們要做模擬的時候 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫了 , 他說 , 只要分析引擎存在 , 它會肯定指導未來科學的未來 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有建造 , 因為他一直在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我會給你們看一些影片 , 說明它看起來像什麼樣子 , 用一部影片來說明它看起來像什麼樣子 , 像是在動作中的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組裝置 , 所以你想像這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年之前 , 我們會有它 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這張圖片中 , 《家人》 , 《家人》 , 在這個圖片中 , 《地球上》 , 《家人》 , 《家人》 , 描述了《地球》 , 《家》 , 《家人》 , 描述了他的《地球》的一部電影 , 《家人》 , 《家人》 , 描述了他的《地球》的一部電影 , 《家人》 , 《家》 , 描述了人類對環境透過呼吸收縮短片拍攝的影片 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人類、媒體、攝影師 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yann藝術husbertrand捕捉到廣泛的全球性 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球上有很大的衝擊 , 以飛機飛行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我排放在大氣層中 , 9噸的二氧化碳 , 是兩個大氣層的大氣層 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態學 , 我在一個法國人一年內生產了二氧化碳 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以我要怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我必須殺掉一位法國人嗎 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來做我的碳排放 , 就像我每次都一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上我的工作是要展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 是我在過去一年所做的一些例子 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	阿爾伯塔沙油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在阿爾伯塔人工作的24小時中 , 七分之二十四小時 , 讓它們能做到 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	油沙不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們用了三倍的石油 , 每年都比我們找到的還要多 。

coral reef in new caledonia .	珊瑚礁在新加州的珊瑚礁 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston , 理查德•雷斯頓的研究中 , 理查•雷斯頓理查德•雷斯頓 , 理查德•雷斯頓 , 理查德•雷斯頓 , 理查德•雷斯頓 , 理查德•雷斯頓 , 理查•雷斯頓
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•安德森:歡迎來到基因體革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我給你們看人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體 , 左邊 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	底部是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩種大型x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性x染色體 ;
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩 , 但這只是一個小小的小東西讓你不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	如果你放大這個基因組 , 你可以看到 , 當然 , 這是雙螺旋結構 , 裡面有四種生物化學字母 , 或我們稱它們為基礎 , 例如:c、g和t 。

daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	danielkraft發明了一個更好的方法來收集骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	所以 , 我是骨髓移植手術 , 我的臨床專注是骨髓移植手術 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	靈感來自jillboltetaylor去年 , 我沒有帶出人類的大腦 , 但我做了一根骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	骨髓其實是我們用來拯救數千名病人的許多人 , 大部分的患者都有先進的乳癌 , 像是白血病 , 和其他疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	幾年前 , 我在史丹佛大學做我的移植工程 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 , 我們有一個博士 , 一個志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他送到全國各地 , 拯救了孩子的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這些骨髓呢 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一個全部麻醉、護士 , 還有另一位醫生在我身邊 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	波布在桌上 , 我們帶著這個小型的針 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們所做的是基本上 , 透過軟組織組織 , 讓它進入硬骨骨髓 , 每次 , 針對十個骨頭 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把牠帶到護士 , 把牠送到海裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把我帶回來 , 我們再一次再次做一次 。
about 200 times usually .	大約兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	在我的手上 , 手上有一支手臂 , 一旦我手上手臂 , 就會看到像瑞士一樣 , 像瑞士一樣 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我想 , 你知道的 , 這個程序已經改變了40年 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想起了最初的一個新的裝置 , 我們稱之為 「 馬爾礦工 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	此外 , 它的運作方式被呈現出來 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們標準的病患 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	不是進入了幾十次的前面 , 我們進入前面的前面 , 或背後的骨頭 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個很有彈性的電池 , 用一種特殊的線路 , 可以繞著一邊的路線 , 繞著它移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它讓你很快地穿過一個洞 , 很快地 , 很快就穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以多次通過相同的動作 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	很快地 , 麻醉劑會吸收一份子宮 , 讓它可以得到一個刺激、地方的麻醉劑 , 並且讓它成為一個專家 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 , 我在史丹佛做了一些原型 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再加上一點點 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到了兩大的動物和豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 很驚人的是 , 我們不只會得到骨髓 , 我們也得到骨髓的幹細胞活動 , 比一般裝置的幹細胞活動還要多 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置是fda的應用程式 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活病患者 , 你可以看到它跟著有彈性的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡有兩位在同一個病患 , 相同的病人 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地麻醉劑中做過的 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	再次 , 我們再次增加了三到六倍的幹細胞 , 比標準處理同樣的病人的幹細胞還要多 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	為什麼你要關心 ? 骨髓是成人幹細胞的主要原因 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很棒的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們的骨髓中培養幹細胞 , 包括我們骨髓裡的幹細胞 , 包括血液幹細胞 , 在我們骨髓裡的幹細胞 , 包括我們骨髓裡的幹細胞 , 包括我們骨髓裡的幹細胞 , 包括我們骨髓中的血幹細胞 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 使用骨髓幹細胞來治療治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病的疾病 , 包括心臟病、血管疾病 , 及糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	今年 , 我們剛剛進來 , 我們已經出版了 , 一代2.0.0.0 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望是讓更多幹細胞變得更好 , 更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人來參加 , 讓更多人成為潛能的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可以讓你銀行自己的幹細胞 , 當你更年輕、更健康 , 用在未來你需要它的時候 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這是我們骨髓移植手術的照片 , 每年在史丹佛大學的照片 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這技術能讓我們有更多的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和surfergarrettlisi提出了一個爭議性的新模型 , 來解釋宇宙的新模型 。 如果沒有其他 , 它是最美麗的八維模型 , 它是你所見過最美麗的最美麗的新模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理 , 科學 , 科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	在他的理論上 , 所有東西的理論 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	誰 , 查出那些殺人的方程式 , 看看那些殺人的方程式 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的18分鐘我要做最好我能描述美麗的粒子物理學沒有方程式
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們能從珊瑚中學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚頭都有數千個單位的珊瑚 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚會會持續不斷地突破 , 與基因相同的鄰居合作 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	假如我們想像這是個超聰明的珊瑚 , 我們就能單獨一個人問他一個問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他如何在這個特定的位置中 , 和他鄰居的鄰居相比 , 如果它有機會 , 或其他的鄰居 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	把溫度太高 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可能是很有意思的 , 你可以看到 , 我有很大的壓力 , 來證明它 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個警察會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居非常明顯地描述他的鄰居 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他在其他的位置也一樣 , 但 , 把它們分離成不同的人 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分散成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 一個非常聰明的珊瑚會很獨特地準備要了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學量子力學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙如何運作 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對人類來說 , 很奇怪 , 因為我們只能經歷一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子怪異 , 是他貓的第一次描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設備中 , 它被放射到一個原始的狀態 , 一種放射性樣本 , 由量子力學的原子所組成 , 它被放射到一個狀態 , 不論是哪個狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個樣本的中間 , 它會被釋放出來 , 釋放毒素和schrodinger死亡 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在其他的領域中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些真相是透過每個人的體驗分開 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	如同所言 , 另一個人並不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為每個人都只經歷一個個人存在 , 我們沒有看到其他的範圍 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	像我們一樣 , 像沙漠一樣 , 正如同一種珊瑚蟲 , 將各種可能性分類成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學量子力學告訴我們這個世界是如何運作的 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以在單一句子裡說:所有事情都能發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不代表一切發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理是描述發生什麼事 , 什麼都無法 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 一切都在幾何學和相互作用 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	如果這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來談談這些粒子 , 了解這些粒子 , 以及這個平衡運作方式 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一個大量的光束 , 和光線聚集在一起 , 產生出一顆巨大的能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這個能量會被轉換成一系列的原子粒子粒子 , 偵測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這種巨大的機器大型鐵粒撞擊器在洛杉磯的大型機械大型鐵子撞擊器 , 當它運作時 , 將五倍的電力轉換為城市蒙特利的機器 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法預測特定的粒子會在任何一個撞擊中產生任何一個撞擊 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子必須有許多質量和能量 , 只由質量和能量所組成 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子比這個能量限制還不夠大 , 還不存在我們 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼新粒子加速器很興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會將這個能量限制七倍 , 所以我們將會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談到之前 , 讓我描述我們所知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	原子粒子有一大堆的原子粒 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	大部分人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這房間裡的許多人 , 很擅長推動他們 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電荷和一個中央的夥伴叫做中央氣體 , 不是電荷和一個非常微小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 大大的質子和中子在原子中形成質子和中子的質子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都在左邊和右撇子 , 和右撇子相反的粒子 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較少熟悉第二代和第三代代代 , 同時也比較熟悉第二代 , 和第三代代代相同 , 相同的粒子也比較不熟悉粒子 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子和各種力量粒子相互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力與電磁力互動 , 電磁力與電磁力互動 , 電磁力與電磁力互動 , 叫做光子 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常弱的力量 , 例如 , 弱勢力 , 與左撇子相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	強大的力量在三種不同的不同種類:紅色、綠色和藍色之間 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪怪的名字是他的錯覺 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 引力的力量是重力的力量 , 與物質的重力相互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 要了解這裡有一種不同的載荷 , 和所有這些力量有關 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這些四種不同的力量與物質相互作用 , 根據對應荷粒有所不同的作用 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個粒子還沒見過 , 但是我們很確定存在 , 希格斯粒子 , 會產生質量 , 和粒子一樣 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子撞擊器的主要目的是要看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎肯定會這樣 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎就是我們所看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要展示給各位一個美好的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們把這些不同的粒子用不同粒子用它們的各種不同的粒子來計算 , 總共有226 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	有很多粒子可以繼續追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	似乎很奇怪 , 自然會有很多元素 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們把它們拿出來 , 有些美麗的模式就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 電荷是三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個夸克結合在一起 , 就會產生一個質子 , 它有一連串的電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 相反的粒子也有相反的作用 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現電荷其實是兩種電荷的組合 , 電荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把這些粒子放在兩維空間的電荷中 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力會互相作用 , 用電磁力和弱勢力互動 , 它會產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 非電力模型 」 , 它在1967年就開始了 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	大部分人都只熟悉電荷 , 而不是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	希格斯在左邊 , 有一個大大的巨大質量並破壞對稱的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它讓弱勢力非常弱 , 讓弱勢力非常弱 , 讓弱勢力非常弱 , 讓弱勢力非常弱弱 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這張圖表中 , 光子的電磁力很大 , 電磁力和電力相互作用 , 在這個圖表中 , 電磁力會不斷地擴張 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被稱為兩維空間的電磁性和弱力 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們能將強力的力量轉換成兩條載荷 , 將它們的載荷轉換成兩載載荷 , 引導它們的引力粒子 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有知粒子的載荷都可以在四維空間中 , 以一個四維空間的基礎設施 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	當粒子互動時 , 自然會維持完美的平衡 , 只要粒子互相作用 , 自然就會維持在完美的平衡四周圍 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和一粒子粒子撞擊 , 它就會產生能量和一連串的能量 , 每四個載荷會引起一顆粒子 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都能被創造出來 , 只要它有同樣的能量和維持一連串的零 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這個弱勢力粒子和它的抗粒子可以在撞擊中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 荷一定總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱粒子可以在電子和螞蟻中 , 再加上1顆粒子 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些模式不僅僅是如此 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 互動是如何發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以把這四維空間放在四維空間中 , 讓更好的觀察強度互相作用 , 這對稱是很棒的 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在一個強大的力量粒子中 , 比如這個綠色 , 一個強力的粒子 , 例如這個綠色 , 用不同顏色的電力粒子組成 , 例如這個紅色 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動在我們體內的每一秒鐘 , 將原子核聚集在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四條曲線對三種力量的影響 , 並不是故事的最後 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也能包含兩種引力力的力量 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們包含這些粒子時 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都在六維空間中 , 產生一個很好的模式 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以把這個模式轉換成六個維度 , 看到它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	現在 , 這個模式將我們最熟悉的知識大自然建立在微小尺寸的宇宙中 。
this is what we know for certain .	這就是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子在非常限制的情況下 , 我們能夠達到實驗 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道粒子物理是非常漂亮的 。 宇宙的運作方式是非常漂亮的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些新的和古老的想法我們不知道
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要擴展這個模式 , 使用數學 , 看看我們能否取得我們的手 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有粒子和力量 , 使我們宇宙的所有粒子組成 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想要用這張圖來預測新粒子 , 我們希望用這個圖來預測新粒子 , 來預測新的粒子 , 我們希望用這個圖來預測新粒子 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 有一個古老的概念 , 粒子在粒子中形成了電磁性 , 可以從一個更完美的模式中 , 可以從更完美的模式中 , 產生電磁性 , 可以從更完美的模式中產生電磁性 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要介紹新的電荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹新方向時 , 我們會猜測荷粒子在哪裡移動 , 然後我們就能和他人一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們猜想 , 我們就能建構在六個荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷荷里 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這種特定的選擇在1973年 , 由巴蒂和薩爾姆在1973年提出了 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們觀察這個新的獨立模式時 , 我們可以看到一些差距 , 粒子似乎被誤解了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是科學工作的理論 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家看起來更大、更大、更大、更大、更大、更大、更具體的結構 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測出存在粒子從未見過的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統計模型預測了這些兩種新力量的存在 , 它應該像弱勢力 , 只有弱勢力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在 , 我們可以把這串載荷帶到七維空間中 , 並考慮一個奇怪的粒子:第二和第三代 , 基本粒子是第二和第三代 , 和第二個第三世代相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不獨特在六個荷荷中分辨出來 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準的電荷空間中 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八維空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以為每一個粒子創造獨特的新荷荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以把這八個維度放進去 , 看看整個模式看起來是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡 , 我們可以看到第二和第三代 , 與第一代相互聯繫的第一代 , 是對稱作 「 三世代 」 的對稱 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八維空間中 , 它是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大規模的典型範例 , 第八名 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言是平滑 , 彎曲的形狀有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	這些圖案的對稱是非常複雜且美麗的形狀 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這八種形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦所謂的 「 重力 」 、解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	用量子力學 , 形狀的幾何形狀可以描述所有宇宙如何運作在最微小的尺度 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這個形狀的形狀存在於八維空間中 , 這形狀是非常美麗的 , 它將數以千計的可能性粒子組成成千上萬種可能的互動 , 這種形狀的形狀是非常美麗的 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉時 , 我們可以看到許多其他的複雜模式包含在這個 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過這個圖案 , 我們可以透過這個圖案 , 看到所有粒子 , 通過這個模式 , 在八度空間中 , 看到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 新的粒子被這個模式所需要 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子有20個差距 , 新粒子有20個落差 , 新粒子是粒子的 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	在這個圖案中 , 我們知道這些新粒子會像希格斯粒子一樣 , 但有顏色和強力 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	在這些新的粒子中 , 把這些新粒子變成了這個模式 , 給予我們全部的8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這八種模式有非常深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被認為是數學中最美麗的結構之一 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的數學美麗可以描述真相對粒子相互作用的真相 , 很棒的數學美麗可以描述真相對粒子相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這個想法 , 自然界的數學並不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的祖本 , 已經寫出了這個: 「 大自然的祖本書 , 一直在數學中被寫成 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形、圓形和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有這些人 , 都無法理解一個單一字 , 不論是誰 , 都無法理解一個單一字 , 不論是誰 , 都無法理解一個字 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是正確的 , 我試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 用三角形、圓形和其他幾何形狀來描述數學粒子物理 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 身為物理學家 , 我真的在做這些東西 , 數學可以組成一個黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但這數學的核心是純粹、美麗的幾何形狀 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入了量子力學 , 這個數學描述了我們宇宙中的粒子 , 透過量子力學 , 這個數學描述宇宙 , 以一種美麗的形式 , 將我們的宇宙轉換成一個美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的模式 , 使用新的機器 , 像是大型強大的電子機械 , 我們可能可以看到大型的電子機械是大型的電子機械 , 我們可能可以看見大型的電子機械是大型的電子機械 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個過程發現的是一個很棒的冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到粒子的粒子 , 那會非常非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 很有趣 , 但不符合這個模式 , 會非常有趣 , 但不符合這個模式 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說 , 很糟糕 。
now how bad would that be ?	那有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 很糟 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測大自然如何運作 , 是非常冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的 , 都是長期的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	很多努力工作都知道大部分的想法可能不會終於大自然 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這就是理論物理學的理論 , 像是:有很多的管道 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新物理理論就像是新物理學理論 , 新物理理論就像是新公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	只要有這麼大的投資 , 就會很難避免在工作時 , 會很難避免 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果你沒有工作 , 你必須去嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 唯一能維持保持和觀點的唯一方式就是保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我嘗試過最好的我能活平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	順便一提 , 儘管我在物理學上工作的一切都沒有 , 我仍然知道我已經活過了好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十多年來 , 我住在馬烏地 , 一個非常漂亮的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	這是宇宙中最偉大的謎題之一 , 是我的父母 , 我如何經常生活 , 卻沒有參與任何完整的職業 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要讓你們看這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我家在maui的觀點 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能注意到這些美麗的觀點相似 , 但在不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	這是因為這習慣於我家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一個非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心租容讓我花時間做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	生活在美麗的環境中 , 但它讓我能活在美麗的地方 , 並且保持平衡 , 讓我生活在美麗的地方 , 並且保持平衡 , 讓我生活在美麗的地方 , 並且保持平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我花了很多時間 , 讓我花很多時間 , 用智力的珊瑚來做 。

ca: it doesn't really matter .	克里斯:這並不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它是一種奇怪的感覺 , 我肯定想要了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但謝謝你來到這裡 , 這絕對是令人驚訝的 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	黑猩猩的研究者珍妮•哈爾談到關於tacare和其他社區計劃 , 幫助人們在非洲城鎮上生存和其他社區的計畫 , 幫助人們在原住民居住的野生動物身上 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、生物多樣性
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍妮•哈拉爾幫助人類和動物活在一起 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 不好 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , 噢 ,
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	那就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺時會做的事 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你從一群小山谷的一角落到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一步 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	我今天想跟各位談談這個晚上 , 從昨天的演講 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他在談的是這個奇妙的三歲小孩 , 伊斯蘭教徒 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過人類的歷史 , 家族樹 , 來自dna基因傳遞的歷史 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是一位古生物學家 , 拉特•萊特 , 他在研究黑猩猩的路上 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	這很不可思議 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	這很普遍 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲的早期人類的抗藥性 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以告訴很多關於那些被從化石上從化石中所看到的形狀 , 那些來自化石的形狀 , 來自化石的形狀 , 來自化石的形狀 , 來自化石的形狀 , 來自化石的形狀 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們怎麼做呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化化 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他現在認為 , 這種行為模式很普遍 , 如同我們最近的親戚一樣 , 很常見的理論 , 如果我們找到行為模式 , 或我們親近親近親近親戚 , 人類的祖先 , 大約七百萬年前的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們從古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看今天的教科書 , 人類進化的行為 , 你通常會發現人們對人類演化的行為有多早的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比其他生物還多 , 我們在ted會議中聽到這個ted會議 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 對我來說 , 黑猩猩和我們一樣 , 牠們的行為是如此的 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有自己的個人性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們名字 , 他們可以活到60歲 , 儘管我們認為大多數人可能不會在野生中六十歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	史黛絲 , 母子在十二歲時 , 雌性第一次寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	每五或六年 , 每五年或六年都很長一段時間 , 孩子的確保持在晚上 , 和媽媽一起睡覺 , 和母親一起睡覺 , 和母親一起睡覺 , 讓她回來 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 這對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 對黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 這對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦變得更複雜 , 在不同的形式動物中 , 我們發現學習扮演著重要的角色 , 以不同形式的角度來看 , 我們發現學習會扮演更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察牠們的生長 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們可以模仿行為的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 我們相信 , 這種方式在不同種類的行為中 , 都是從一個世代到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、限制 , 和練習 , 讓我們能夠描述這些行為 , 成為原始文化的行為 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有語言 , 我們已經談過 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們有非常豐富的生存和姿勢 , 許多相似的 , 甚至是相似的 , 甚至是相似的 , 甚至是相似的 , 甚至在同一個情境中 , 也有相似之處 , 甚至在相同的情況下 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	它們也吻合 , 雙手 , 把手放在後面 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	然後他們把搖滾滾滾 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們找到許多相同的例子 , 鼓勵愛和真實的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們像我們一樣 , 牠們喜歡我們 , 牠們有黑暗的面向 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們是非常殘酷的 , 甚至是一個原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些真正的行為 , 對大部分的部分來說 , 都是對鄰居社會團體的行為 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們是非常精彩的活動 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比任何其他生物都能幫助我們了解 , 人類和其他動物王國之間沒有鯊魚 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	它是非常模糊的 , 隨著我們做更多的觀察 , 就會變得越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究 , 一直持續到今天 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩 , 牠們的複雜社群生活在野外 , 讓我們了解到我們是一部分 , 而非分離 , 與我們分享地球的動物有多大 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 要找到黑猩猩 , 就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 都會失去自己的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這張照片是從空氣中拍攝的 , 它向你展示森林的高島 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	當時我在六年前 , 發現在公園的東岸 , 當時我在公園裡 , 發現在公園的森林中 , 當時我在公園裡 , 大約十六年前 , 發現在公園裡 , 這種森林 , 大約16年前 , 發現在公園的森林裡 , 這種森林在公園裡出現了很大的差距 , 一個問題來到我腦海裡 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 , 當人們住在國家公園時 , 那些有名的黑猩猩 , 當人們居住在國家公園時 , 他們會怎麼做 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多的人住在地面上 , 比陸地還能支持 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	數量增加了 , 來自土地的數量 , 比來自布朗克斯和湖邊的數量更高 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人他們無法負擔得起買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 tacare 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常合理的方式 , 可以改善生活在公園裡的人的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	從小到12個村莊 , 現在是24歲 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間去進去 , 但它包含了一些像樹木護士一樣 , 幾乎沙漠的土地在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制 , 防止土壤消耗 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重建農田的土地 , 在兩年之內 , 牠們可以再次做生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	為了幫助村民 , 能協助村民取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些學校 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與小群婦女合作 , 提供他們機會給微貸貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	而我們就在世界各地 , 大約百分之九十五的貸款都是貸款 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性教育 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 讓女性教育改善 , 家庭大小的花費 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供關於家庭計畫和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這項計畫的結果是為了保育 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的重點是 , 農民住在24個村莊裡 , 但當我們開始計劃時 , 農民們住在這24個村莊裡 , 而不是看著我們 , 成為村落裡的農民 , 看著我們 , 成為村落裡的農民 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	它是坦尚尼亞團隊和村民們談話 , 問他們對什麼感興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育有興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間進步 , 他們開始了解更多關於保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 在山丘上的高樓層面是樹木 , 所以你有了很糟糕的土壤和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在開發出我們所謂的 「 更大的發展 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是在國家公園的地位 , 把它們放大到全國公園 , 延伸到所有這些非常嚴重的土地 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	隨著這些村莊有更好的標準 , 他們真的同意將在公園裡的百分之二十的土地上有更好的標準 , 這樣一來 , 當這些村莊有更好的標準 , 他們真的同意將這些村莊有更好的標準 , 讓它們能夠與其他的獨立居民一起交流 , 來交互相互作用 , 如樹木長回來 , 黑猩猩會有更好的標準 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們還在非洲其他地方 , 其他的地區 , 和極端人口壓力有關 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 在非洲 , 我們一直討論過的問題 , 是主要的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	這裡有很大的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你在土地上大量的人口砍伐樹木時 , 會發生什麼事 ? 要做些什麼 ? 要做些什麼 ? 要做些什麼 ? 要怎麼做 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	另外一個問題不僅是非洲 , 還有其他的問題 , 不僅是非洲 , 還有其他的問題 , 包括開發中國家 , 以及我們在哪裡做的事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	各位知道 , 傑出的科學家 , 艾倫•威爾森說 , 如果每個人在這個星球上 , 只有三個新的行星 , 我們就需要三個新的行星 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說了四個 。 但我們沒有他們 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 在這裡 , 我們是世界上最有智慧的人 , 可以用這種非凡的大腦 , 來處理這些ted會議 , 並且我們還會被這些ted會議所引發 , 並且我們還會被這些ted會議所引發 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決策之前 , 會問自己: 「 這決定如何影響我們七代前代的人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 主要的決策不是特別談論非洲 , 而是開發中國家主要的決策 , 包括數百萬人 , 通常是基於: 「 這會如何影響下一個股東的朋友 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決策影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始旅行非洲各地的許多非洲問題時 , 我意識到 , 許多非洲的問題 , 都能被黑猩猩和他們消失的森林砍伐 , 我了解更多 , 很多非洲的問題 , 都可以被黑猩猩和他們消失的森林砍伐 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始旅行非洲 , 在歐洲 , 談話 , 談到美國 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都是這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你們知道我在談的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球是污染我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水水可能是最關鍵的問題之一 , 我們在這個世紀中所看到的 , 包括農業、工業、工業和家庭的化學物質 , 在這個世紀中 , 無法從過去的經驗中獲取 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林已經被砍掉了 , 像海嘯的效應變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤問題 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有無數的燃料和其他溫室氣體排放 , 所以 , 叫做 「 氣候變遷 」 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在世界各地 , 大家都開始相信 , 我們的氣候變遷會造成很大的影響 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候混合在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	貧窮的人會影響更糟 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱變得更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季發生時 , 通常會導致洪水、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在一個地區的人口數量 , 沒有人住在這個地區 , 讓人們無法離開 , 因為整個土地都被降低了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化的結果 , 隨著樹木中的最後一棵樹被砍掉 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不僅僅是非洲 , 而是世界各地 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 讓我感到驚訝的是 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多年輕人似乎失去希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為可能有某種差異的大腦 , 關於愛和同情心的大腦 , 這種特別聰明的大腦 , 這種特別聰明的大腦呢 ? 關於愛和同情心 , 卻沒有人心嗎 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們說 , 不論是憂鬱、或同情、憤怒 , 和他們說 , 基本上 , 他們都說不見 , 不論是憂鬱、或同性戀 , 或同情 , 我們感覺到他們 , 因為我們覺得你對它有所貢獻 。
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥善了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們時 , 我感覺到這個美麗的星球 , 每當我看著他們 , 我就會覺得這美麗的星球 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這引發了這個計畫 , 我們稱之為根源和芽 , 它開始在坦尚尼亞現在散播到97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它有象徵性 , 根源是符合的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊是很小的 , 可以破壞牆壁 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	看看磚牆 , 如我們所在地球上的所有這些問題 , 環境和社會 , 是希望的 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界有數以千計的年輕人 , 可以讓這個更好的世界變得更好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根源和射擊的重要訊息是:每個人每一天都能改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 , 每個人在這個房間裡 , 我們都有選擇 , 每個人都在這個房間裡 , 我們有選擇 。 每個人在這個房間裡 , 我們都有選擇 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的選擇 , 沒有選擇 。 我們要改變事物 , 讓窮人有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根和芽團體都選了三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	它取決於他們是哪個國家 , 無論是城市或鄉村 , 還是鄉村 , 都在城市或鄉村 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們有了從幼稚園到大學的課程 , 越來越多成年人開始自己的根源和槍枝 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體選擇 , 三種不同的不同問題 , 互相連結和互相連結 , 並且彼此互相連結 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們的計畫之一是要幫助他們自己的人類社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	接著 , 如果他們能幫助社區 , 他們可能會募集資金來幫助全世界的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項計畫會幫助動物 , 不只是野生動物 , 也是動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一個計畫是要幫助我們周遭的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	所有這一切都是學習的訊息 , 在我們的家庭中 , 在我們的社區中 , 在我們的家庭 , 在我們的社區 , 宗教之間 , 在我們的社區中 , 在我們的家庭中 , 在我們的社區中 , 在我們的家庭中 , 在我們的社區中 , 在我們的社區中 , 宗教與我們之間之間的關係 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 , 我們不能去摧毀它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有比這個星球還要多 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要挑選一或兩項計畫 , 在非洲 , 加州 , 南非 , 加薩維爾 , 南非 , 加拿大 , 南非 , 加薩維爾 , 南非 , 加薩維爾 , 南非 , 加薩維爾 , 南非 , 加州 , 南非 , 加州 , 南非 , 加州 , 南非 , 加州 , 南非 , 兩項專案 。 我說 , 世界上有97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們正在種植樹木 , 它們正在成長有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營裡工作 , 把雞蛋花在難民營裡 , 吃雞蛋 , 賺錢 , 或只是為了賺錢 , 給他們賺錢 , 或只是用他們來餵養他們的家人 , 覺得自己有幸福 , 卻沒有幫助 , 並依賴別人的飲食和雞肉 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理協助 , 來給予一些心理幫助 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的計畫 , 把他們自己放出來 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄裡也有這樣的計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 沒有時間 , 更多的根和芽 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在愛滋病工作 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	這是根源和槍枝的一部分 , 老年的孩子們跟年輕人談話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而非成年人 , 而非成年人 , 而非成年人 , 而不是成人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 , 這是我被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過你看過太多恐怖的事情 , 你看到了黑猩猩的數量 , 已經超過150 , 000次 , 和其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 森林消失了 , 森林消失了 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 可以嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 有希望 。 一個是人類的大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	想想看科技 。

it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我最喜歡的其中之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們把所有的水放到水下 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	再來談談再生能源是很重要的 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們在乎地球嗎 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有孩子或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們關心他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 身為世界各地的人 , 我們可以做些什麼 。 我們可以做些什麼 。 我們可以做些什麼 。 我們可以做出選擇 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買了什麼 , 我們買的東西 。

so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 和人類的心臟合作 , 我們加入世界各地 。

all of these technologies we can use .	我們所能使用的技術 。

this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這改變 , 改變 , 若我們在乎未來 , 就會改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望大自然的下一個理由 , 希望大自然是神奇的 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一個區域完全被摧毀 , 或許有些協助可以再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	一個例子是tacare計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴你們 , 如果你停止砍伐木材 , 你不需要因為你有樹木 , 你就不需要因為你有30英呎的樹木 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	動物 , 幾乎在滅絕的狀態下一本書 , 可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它啟發了我 , 帶著我過去兩天:這可憐的人類精神 , 大家認為會被貧窮、疾病、或疾病所影響 , 或任何人 , 可以把他們自己放在社會中 , 並且把他們帶到社會中 , 並且將他們帶入社會中 , 並且將他們帶到世界各地 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想看一個或兩位非洲的人 , 真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以做一個很長的清單 , 但很顯然 , 尼爾森•曼德拉 , 17年來了 , 很長的清單 , 所以他可以領導他的國家 , 不管是種族隔離的種族隔離 , 沒有血球 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	kensarowiwa , 在奈及利亞 , 在奈及利亞 , 在奈及利亞的大型石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人都嘗試他們最好的做法 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是如此靈感 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的我們需要年輕非洲人的角色模型 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們需要一些環境的角色模型 , 我今天聽過一些 。

and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望有些人能聚在一起討論這些東西 , 特別是根源和槍枝計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個詞 , 今天我遇見了她 , 今天我遇見她 。

and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 非常令人興奮 , 讓我看到一個例子 , 一個年輕人 , 當他們被賦予權力 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 我們希望明天 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家迪納•柯芬分享了一些關於塑膠污染的真相 , 關於塑膠污染的真相 , 我們的生活中有一些關於塑膠污染的真相 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、藍色、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	狄安娜•柯林:對塑膠污染的真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是個視覺藝術家 , 我也是其中一位視覺藝術家 , 我也是一種塑膠污染聯盟的共同創作 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直和塑膠袋一起工作 , 把我和塑膠袋放在一起 , 用塑膠袋 , 把我切割成三十年來的主要材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成兩、三維空間、雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	過去八年來 , 我的工作開始分裂成小小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 很好 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	像我們一樣 , 像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	更進一步 , 我意識到這是個壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分裂成小小一點點 , 因為它一直都是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們在海洋環境中發現很多 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	在過去幾年 , 我了解到太平洋垃圾和蓋爾 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是: 「 噢 ! 我的天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須走出去 , 去清理這些東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我真的開發了一個建議 , 要用一台車牌 , 一台車牌 , 一台車牌 , 一台車牌 , 一台車牌 , 一台車牌 , 一台車牌 , 一台飛船 , 兩艘船員 , 一台飛行器 , 一台火車飛行器 , 一台飛行器 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意見是 , 開始拿起塑膠 , 把塑膠拆掉 , 把塑膠放到小小的垃圾桶裡 , 把塑膠變成小小的垃圾桶 , 把塑膠變成小小的垃圾桶 , 把塑膠變成小小的垃圾桶 , 把塑膠變成小小的垃圾桶 , 把塑膠變成小小的垃圾桶 , 把塑膠變成小小的垃圾桶 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和人們談談 , 實際上 , 我需要回頭看更大的圖片 , 看看更大的圖像 , 實際上我需要回頭看看更大的圖片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的圖片是:我們需要找到一種方法 , 來避免疫苗 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切斷這些塑膠 , 進入海洋環境 , 每天都在全球規模上 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看看這一點 , 我也發現我很憤怒 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我並不擔心塑膠 , 可能是塑膠在世界上五個大海裡的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不僅僅是塑膠的塑膠 , 我很擔心它是塑膠的商品 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我來到超市 , 所有的食物都包裝在塑膠裡 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的平均都包裝在塑膠裡 , 甚至是健康食物市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關注了塑膠和毒素從塑膠和毒素從塑膠變成我們的身體
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以 , 我和一群人一起研究這個議題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多計畫 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果80到90%我們在海洋中看到的海洋中發現的海洋是塑膠 , 那為什麼我們不稱它為它 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收所有人的書 , 都是永續和綠色的回收方式 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放進一個罐子裡 , 你不需要再思考一次 。

in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 不到7%的塑膠被回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你仔細看 , 尤其是當它進入塑膠瓶時 , 大部分只會下降 , 或被送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被循環 , 塑膠瓶可以再一次塑膠瓶 , 再一次塑膠瓶 , 再也不會再塑膠瓶子 。

phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里茲和安德里茲•羅德里茲在阿爾瓦菲的國際貿易中心攻擊中被殺死了 。 艾薩克•羅德里茲在191年9月11日被殺死了 , 這兩位媽媽都來找和平 , 兩位媽媽都來找和平 , 所有人都在尋找和平 , 這兩隻媽媽都來了解與尊重 。

before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在生活品之前 , 最好的手濾器只能在200奈米的水下降到大約200奈米 。

so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌會通過200奈米的細菌 。

so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	這絕對是從200奈米的洞中得到的 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生活品質是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	一切都沒有發生 。

there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在十九世紀末期 , 詩人寫了一首詩 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 教科爾的腦袋裡的大腦 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是: 「 夏天 , 我聽到一個很棒的歌曲 , 很快就死了 。 」 我聽到一個鼓舞 , 很快就死去 , 像是在夢裡的小說 , 很快就會死去 , 說: 「 夏天 , 我聽到一個很棒的聲音 , 很快就會死去 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩人有興趣的詩人是 「 shropsman 」 , 詩是 「 shropsman 」 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但馬尼爾斯曼明白 , 你聽見它 , 尤其是當權力改變時 , 十九世紀的西班牙人 , 很長、很熱 , 西班牙文明的年輕人 , 很久 , 熱 , 西班牙文明的年輕人 , 很快就要進入其中一個令人驚訝的歷史 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	各位先生女士 , 女士們先生們 , 全都穿過血液 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	而我的信息是 , 如果你喜歡 , 生活在這個世界的新勢力的新勢力 , 在這個世界的新勢力 , 開始改變和新勢力的新勢力 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	我們現在看到的很顯然 , 幾乎總是非常嚴重的時期 , 通常是非常嚴重的時期 , 通常是非常嚴重的時期 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便一提 , 每世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會說 , 最後一次發生了 , 當權力來自舊的國家 , 歐洲的大西洋 , 全新的新興起美國國家的力量 , 歐洲的大西洋 , 到美國最新的新興起力量 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在那一刻 , 歐洲權力被用來扮演了兩個偉大的戰爭 , 一部分是兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	麥歐文戰爭 , 可能更準確地描述它們 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在其中一個時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我想談談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 這兩者 , 重點是要改變權力 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於一些新的維度我想要從未發生過的新維度
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談改變權力的轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的情況是 , 很恐怖的是 , 因為從來沒有發生過 。

and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	也就是說 , 國家獨立與其他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 。
