that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	當敵人在牆壁時 , 敵人是外面 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人在牆壁中 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我要談談國內的安全 , 我必須和政府談談 , 因為流行病對我來說是安全的威脅 , 我必須和政府談談 , 因為流行病對我來說是安全的威脅 , 我必須和政府談談 , 因為流行病對我來說是安全的威脅 , 我必須和政府談談 , 因為流行病對我來說是安全的威脅 , 我必須和國內的官員談談 , 因為流行病是一種威脅 , 我必須和國內的官員談談 , 因為流行病對我的國家有直接影響 , 就像我們在倫敦看到的 , 要談到國內的防禦 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	它不再是美國國家的安全 , 一個國家的安全只是為了它的軍人和國防部的安全 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力可以鎖在一起它的制度 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴各位 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 建構出了錯誤的結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	你在商業知道我們時間的典型結構 , 女士們先生們就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	你的能力可以網路重要 , 包括你的政府和外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是第三條法律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 如果有第三條法律 , 不要問我先生的第一條法律 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	第三條法則是 , 在現代時代 , 所有東西都連結在一起 , 最重要的事情是你能和其他人做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的是 , 你的權力 , 不論你是企業 , 不管你是企業 , 不管你是企業 , 你的關係 , 你的關係 , 不管你是企業 , 你的關係 , 和其他人的關係 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你知道在產業中 , 政府沒有 。
but now one final thing .	但 , 最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	假如各位 , 女士們 , 先生們 , 我們現在與彼此相同 , 先生們 , 這也是我們與彼此之間的關係 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 第一次 , 集體防禦 , 首次 , 被迫使我們國家的概念 , 不再足夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 我是安全的 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 , 我是安全的 , 我是安全的 , 我是安全的 , 我是安全的 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	它不再是這樣 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互聯繫和武器的大規模毀滅性武器是如此 , 我與敵人之間的關係 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	我在1970年代 , 與蘇聯聯合國會議院談判時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和蘇聯共享了他們 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全並不足夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平剛來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為兩邊都知道 , 零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人分享了命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東地區最棒的障礙之一 , 和平在中東地區是兩邊 , 和平的 , 都是以色列和平 , 但我認為 , 巴勒斯坦人並不了解他們共享集體的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以突然間 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 最後就結束了 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐納的一首詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要把貝殼賣出來 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是一個島嶼 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它會說: 「 每個人的死亡都會影響我 , 不論是誰 , 都會影響我 , 不論是誰是誰 , 都會影響我 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	約翰•唐納 , 是道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 為我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到路徑長壽、健康、丹佛頓和世界的藍色區塊 , 會說: 「 藍色區塊 」 社群 , 長壽命和維京人都在tedxttner和團隊研究這個世界: 「 藍色區塊 , 」 社群 , 生長壽命和健康 , danbuettner和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區塊 」 , 他們在tedxttner和團隊研究這個世界: 「 藍色區塊 」 , 六十歲時 , 他共享了九種共同飲食和生活方式 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuett:如何活到100+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	一個叫做丹尼•泰丁的研究 , 只有10%長久以來 , 人類生活在某些生物限制中 , 我們的基因會被遺傳 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十的是我們生活方式 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍色區塊的最佳方式:如果我們能找到最佳的壽命長壽 , 我們能找到最適合的壽命長壽 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問平均壽命的最佳形式 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或是皮膚飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	醫生奧茲告訴我們 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	重點是 , 有很多困惑 , 讓我們更好的更好 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該要跑馬拉松或做瑜伽嗎 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	應該吃有機肉 , 或應該吃有機肉嗎 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當它來到供應時 , 應該要拿它們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙或逆轉會如何呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的的目的不是嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神性嗎 ? 我們如何社會化 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	嗯 , 我們的方法是與國家地理協調合作 , 找到四個人口統計 , 來找出四個人口統計 , 來找出四個人口統計 , 來找出四個人口統計的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 把一個專家的專家帶進去 , 將這些人所做的事 , 轉變為全部的專家 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位 , 這種分裂是什麽 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想要破解一些常見的迷思 , 直到長壽時 , 才會出現 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你嘗試非常困難 , 你可以活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 僅僅在美國有5000人 , 只有15000人住在100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是美國最快的人口統計數字 , 很難達到100個 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們沒有程式要長壽 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被稱為 「 成功的成功 」 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒了我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家成功的意思是 , 當你的孩子有孩子時 , 年齡 , 你的孩子有孩子時 , 就會有孩子的命運 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	經過演化的效果之後 , 演化完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是哺乳動物 , 或大象 , 或人類 , 相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要到達100歲 , 你不只需要有很好的生活方式 , 你也必須取得基因學 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 治療可以幫助緩慢、反轉 , 或甚至停止衰老 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想到它時 , 有99個東西可以讓我們 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	將你的腦細胞死掉 , 再回來 , 那些腦細胞死了 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩耍太硬了 , 你膝蓋上 , 無法再回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的大腦可以發揮作用 。 我們的大腦可以穿上皮膚 , 我們的大腦可以穿上皮膚 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要走錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 和 「 t 」 , 我們在談論國家債務 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	每八年來 , 這種細胞就會自動一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己丟到某些損傷後 , 就會損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它建構出了數量 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有些時候 , 像垃圾一樣 , 我們都能打造一套錄音機 , 讓朋友複製一套很快的代碼 , 讓朋友複製一套很快的代碼 , 讓朋友複製一套很快的代碼 , 讓朋友複製一套很快的代碼 , 讓朋友複製一套很快的代碼 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼65倍的速度比十二歲的老人還快十二歲 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有任何東西可以減緩老化或停止你的衰老 , 我在做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實是 , 最重要的是科學告訴我們 , 人類身體的能力 , 身體 , 大概90年 , 更為女性 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家的預期壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	在這條線上 , 我們要留下大約12個好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們能做到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示他們會多年大慢性疾病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為最好的方法就是去看這些世界的文化 , 讓這些年齡死亡的數年 , 比我們所知的還要多 , 中年壽命的人口數年 , 年齡死亡率高達10倍 , 比我們所知的還要多 , 中年齡死亡率是三十倍 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現了我們第一個藍色區域 , 大約125英里 , 位於西亞的海岸 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約是140萬人 , 但只有在高地上 , 島嶼就有一千四百萬人 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	在這裡 , 我們有這個區域 , 住在最長的地區 , 比我們在美國的百分之七十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方不僅僅到達100歲 , 他們也做得很棒 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡102歲的老年人仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 樹木 , 還能打開比他們更年輕的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實回到了關於基督教的歷史 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是一堆古老的文化 , 被孤立了 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地的土地很高 , 大部份是牧羊 , 主要是牧羊 , 大量的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是植物為基礎的食物 , 他們的飲食可以帶到田野 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	牠們出發了一大堆牛肉 , 叫做卡卡塔音樂 , 由灰色動物組成的 , 這種葡萄酒 , 比任何知道葡萄酒的大麥有三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正秘密我認為謊言是他們組織社會的秘密 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會的一部份是他們對老人的看法 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你們有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎是24歲嗎 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 老人有更多的智慧 , 你能得到更多的智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你在沙丁尼亞看到一個月曆 , 而不是看到月曆的百分之九 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 對於孩子們的家庭而言 , 這些家庭的壽命比較低 , 不只適合他們的父母 , 還能讓父母親近親戚的壽命率 , 更低率的死亡率和低率疾病 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現了第二個藍色區塊在地球的另一邊 , 大約800英里南 , 阿基蘭加州北部 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主要島嶼的北部 , 這是地球的四分之一 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這裡是最古老的居住女性族群 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這是一個地方 , 人們在世界上最長的壽命不足 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活著很長的時間 , 很快地 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性別之後 , 很快就會死亡 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比美國人平均壽命更長 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍的美國人 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	十五分之一的乳癌、乳癌、乳癌 , 大殺人在美國 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的四分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	這種文化讓這些數字建議很強烈 , 讓他們能教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 植物的飲食含有許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了大約八倍的美國人 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	更重要的是他們吃的是什麼 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種各式各樣的策略來避免 , 如你所知 , 這是美國最大的問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察的其中一些策略是:他們吃掉較小的盤子 , 所以他們會吃少數的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	不是服務家人 , 把食物放到桌子上 , 然後把食物帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有三千歲的年齡 , 我認為這是最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	由於混亂而發明 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為 「 哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、哈拉 」
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	只是一個簡單的說法 , 有人說在他們的餐廳裡 , 要提醒他們不要吃掉他們的胃 , 只剩下10% 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	它花了半小時 , 才能從你的腦袋中傳送到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	只要記住停止80% , 就能幫助你繼續做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像薩丁亞 , okinia , okinawa有一些社會建構 , 讓我們能與長壽相關聯繫 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立殺死了 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	五年前 , 平均美國有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在就到達一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運 , 出生在科納瓦 , 你出生在一個系統中 , 你出生於一個系統 , 你出生在五十個多數的朋友中 , 你出生在你的人生中 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai 。 如果你在moai , 你總是有一份工作 , 如果你是一名運動員 , 你總是有一位人 , 會有你的背後 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這種特殊的母親 , 五位女士已經一起九十七年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	有一天 , 我們退休 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	一般來說 , 它的意思是要退休 , 到亞利桑那州的高爾夫球場 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在科納瓦語中 , 沒有一個字可以退休 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	反而有一句話是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	粗糙地翻譯 , 意思是 「 你早上醒來的原因 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	在這102歲的大師 , 他kigaikigai正在帶著這個巨大的藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這個百歲的漁民而言 , 他的漁夫每週都要持續捕魚 , 數百歲的漁民 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 美國國會議員會提出一個問題 , 給予我們一個問題 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們非常文化化 , 人們會問他們 , 他們是非常文化的 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們很早就知道為什麼他們在早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對於這個102歲的女性 , 她的伊基吉利只是她曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩分離在101年半年 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 覺得自己會覺得什麼樣子 ?
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把她的頭頭放回來 , 她說: 「 感覺就像跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我編輯的編輯在地理想找美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	一旦我們去看了尼蘇達州 , 那裡有非常高的百分之七十 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們把資料再加上了 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們找到美國最長壽的人口 , 大約有七天之內 , 加州在羅馬林達 , 加州 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	傳統主義者是保守派的 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們慶祝他們慶祝了星期六週五週日的聖經節目 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	《24小時的週期》 , 他們稱之為 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循了五個小習慣 , 讓他們很長壽 , 相對的 , 比較說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但 , 身為一位女性 , 他們的壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差異甚至更為人知 , 他們預期壽命比美國人還要長久多久 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這個研究顯示了約七萬人的三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	研究中 , 我認為它很明顯地說明了這個藍色區塊計畫的預期 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個很大的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	白人、黑人、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共同點是一組非常小的生活型習慣他們遵循儀式的習慣
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們把他們的飲食直接從聖經中 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	文字:章魚 , 三分之一的綠色植物 , 通常是肉類 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們在時間非常嚴肅時 , 認真看待這件事 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們是多麼忙碌 , 他們會把焦點放在上帝 , 社交網路 , 然後 , 在宗教上 , 大自然行走 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量的力量是每週都沒有做過 , 即時 , 權力已經完成了 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	不需要錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	傳統主義者也傾向於其他的冒險者 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去一個阿德派的派對你看不見人們穿著jimbeam或rollingjimbeam
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們說的是他們的下一天的自然步行 , 是的 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們影響彼此對彼此的影響 , 以更加深遠的方式 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 讓ellswhareharehareham 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellswhareharehareham97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是個多百萬富翁 , 但當收入者想要6 , 000美元去建立隱私權利時 , 他說: 「 這樣我才能做我自己 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以 , 接下來三天他出了一陣子 , 包圍著四周圍繞著 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預測的是 , 也許 , 在第四天他結束了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是在桌上的人 , 做開頭手術 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	在97歲時 , 每個月都有20個開頭手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	老鼠 , 十三歲 , 一隻活躍的牛仔褲 , 每天早上游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡把板子丟進去 , 丟下樓梯 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子住在雙胞胎城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從那天起起 , 開始了重量 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在聖貝納丁州的洛杉磯 , 在那裡 , 她仍然志願了七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經在19個艱難的旅程 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一你會遇見的人 , 他在撒哈拉沙漠沒有陽光的路上走過沙漠 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我會告訴你們 , 沒有冒險的冒險 , 比起火星高峰還要高 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是個朋友 , 我還沒見過 。 」 她跟我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中有什麼共同點子呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們所做的一切是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	然後我們把它降到九點 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們做了兩種藍色區塊 , 從這些共同的點子中 , 都已經完成了兩種藍色區域 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我要把這段影片放在一起 , 不論是誰 , 至少我們認為運動的運動 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們設立了自己的生命 , 讓它們不斷地被增長到身體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的女兒們在地面上坐下 , 坐著地板、30、40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子 , 樓梯上樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每一趟旅程、教堂、或教堂或教堂 , 或去教堂或去教堂 , 或是去教堂或去教堂 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何的制度 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 去做房子工作或家工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	這種燃燒的卡路里可用在跑步機上 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做實體活動時 , 他們都傾向於走路 , 唯一的證明方式是要走路 , 唯一的證明方式是要走路 , 唯一的證明方式是要走路 , 唯一的證明方式是要走路 , 唯一的證明方式是要走路 , 唯一的證明方式是要走路 , 唯一的證明方式是要走路 , 唯一的證明方式是要走路 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何在正確的環境中找到正確的權利 , 所以他們有正確的權利 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每種文化都需要時間轉變 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 七天的祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawan有這種祖先的祖先 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在受傷或壓力時 , 會觸發出一種叫做 「 炎反應 」 的反應 , 它與所有來自阿茲海默症患者有關的疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你慢慢十五分鐘時 , 你就會轉動到一個更加刺激的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有多樣的特性 , 像是科納瓦語 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你人生中最危險的一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 年復一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的人生 , 值得約七年的壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝了一小部分 , 不是賣給美國人的 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們不會吃肉 , 而是很多豆類和甜蜜 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略 , 讓它們從桌子上移動 , 讓它們從桌子上移動 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接下來的基礎是他們如何聯繫 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把他們的家人拿來 , 照顧他們的孩子和老年人 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都屬於信仰基礎社群 , 值得4、4、14年的壽命 , 只要你花四年的時間 , 才會有四倍的壽命 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 它們也屬於對部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們是生長的 , 或他們將自己與對人的關係連結在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從fm研究中學到 , 如果你三位最好的朋友都肥胖 , 你就會有50%的機會 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你與不健康的人交配 , 那將會有很大的影響力 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你的朋友喝了一小小的飲料 , 或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝了一小塊 , 沒有太多 , 或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝了一小塊 , 但不太多 , 他們就會有很大的影響力 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食不在歷史上 , 世界各地的人口數量超過百分之二 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	練習通常是用十月來完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	長期來說 , 沒有短期的壽命 , 不用藥丸或其他東西 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你思考一下 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 或許你所能做的最重要的事情 , 就是要花更多年的時間去生活 , 非常感謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	用這東西來做實驗 , 卡塔里娜•莫塔里納莫塔里納莫塔里納莫塔里納莫塔里納莫塔里納motarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotari
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarina:
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一位朋友 , 在葡萄牙的家人 , 他可以交通他的家人 , 用腳踏車和洗衣機來運送他的家庭 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他知道如何建造一個 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	有時候 , 我們了解事物如何運作 , 以及它們如何運作 , 所以我們可以建造、修復它們 , 或至少在做些什麼是如何製造的 , 才能建造和修復它們 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀中 , 許多人在20世紀就失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 創作家族群和開放原始碼的模型就是把這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 創造出我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 來說明它們是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何運作的 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分部份 , 我們仍然知道傳統材料像是紙、紡織品 , 以及它們如何生產的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚訝的成果 , 製造電力的塑膠 , 顏色的塑膠 , 會改變形狀 , 顏色的塑膠會改變形狀 , 顏色的塑膠會改變顏色 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我舉個例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	電路板可以用傳統印刷電路板或電路板或電路板 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在這個小小的例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸碰感應器 , 用它來創造一個觸碰感應器 , 用它來創造一個觸碰感應器 , 用它來創造一個觸碰感應器 , 用它來創造一個觸碰感應器 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家最近開發的指標 , 但最近的發展顯示我們很快就能夠用在雷射印表機和鉛筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一顆晶片 , 含有無色無色的紫外線光粒 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 當一般的光線穿過整個表面時 , 我會把光線轉換成光線 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這種材料包含了內部設計和多觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	用溫度的顏色來改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個熱板上 , 一個溫度只能稍微高一點 , 且你可以看到發生了什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	其中一個原則是 , 在嬰兒瓶子裡 , 會讓內容很酷 , 可以喝下去喝 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一些常常被稱為智慧材料的材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年來 , 它們會在日常生活中使用的物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行汽車科幻小說 , 但我們可以有牆壁 , 改變顏色的溫度、鍵盤、鍵盤 , 並且窗戶會轉變為光線 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是一個社會科學家 , 所以為什麼我今天要來談智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是作家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇他們是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何運作的 , 但也是因為我相信我們應該更深入了解 , 創造出我們的世界 , 而現在 , 我們並不知道這些高科技的組合 , 是我們的未來會被製造出來的 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	聰明的材料在小量中很難取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以使用它們 , 很少是說他們如何生產 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 大部分都存在於貿易秘密和專利 , 只有大學和企業都能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年前 , 我開始了一個專案叫做開放材料
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是個網站 , 每個人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 ,
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們會把它變成大型集體的資料庫 , 用智慧型材料來製造資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但 , 為什麼我們要照顧聰明的材料 , 以及他們所做的是什麼 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的事物 , 以及我們無法形塑我們不了解的東西 , 以及我們無法形塑我們不了解的東西 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的東西 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 我們所穿的衣服 , 我們所使用的衣服 , 我們所使用的衣服 , 我們所使用的衣服 , 我們所使用的衣服 , 我們所使用的衣服 , 衣服我們生活
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要活在一個充滿智慧型材料的世界中 , 我們應該知道 , 了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 創新一直都是由tinkerer所組成的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 演員、個人電腦、飛機 , 都沒有專家 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但這並不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾州大學的兩位科學家 , 他們發表了一篇論文 , 用一個簡單的方法來製造出版紙 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他沒有經歷過化學 , 直到那之後 , 讀了這篇文章 , 用它的材料和工具來完成實驗 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用了一個烤箱 , 他甚至製造了自己的創作 , 由另一個科學家/maker所創造的 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	jordan在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過的結果 , 沒有工作 , 所以其他人可以研究並繁殖它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	喬丹的主要創新是 , 在芝加哥使用唯一便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他自己自己 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這項工作 , 其他人可以挑選他出版的作品 , 其他人可以挑選他出版的作品 , 其他人可以選擇留下和改善的過程 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子我要提倡她專注於創造力和技能的創造力和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置非常強大 , 讓他們教導我們學習如何運作 , 但限制在他們教導我們學習如何運作時 , 電子裝置非常強大 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	漢娜的另一方面 , 就是建立一個系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 來協助我們創造出不尋常的物品 , 來協助我們創造出不尋常的物品 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 來協助我們創造出不尋常的物品 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	漢納多令人印象深刻的實驗 , 這是我最喜歡的之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的是一張紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一些銅板 ,
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據研究 , 漢娜颶風的一系列的論文 , 用簡單的銅板來製造一系列的紙 , 用簡單的銅板來製造出一系列的紙 , 用簡單的銅板來製造出一系列的紙張 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他作家一樣 , 漢娜出版了她的教材 , 讓任何人能夠複製並繁殖它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是材料科學中最承諾的材料科學之一 , 它讓我們能創造更便宜且有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的創作者 , 和創新的一系列新可能性 , 都是美好的、創新的 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 創造出熱情和好奇心的好奇心 , 我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常處理問題來自非傳統的角度 , 而在過程中 , 最終發現了替代方案或甚至更好的方法來做事情 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 更多的研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造出自己的知識 , 更好的機會 , 就能創造出科技 , 讓更多的研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造出他們的知識 , 更好的機會 , 才能創造出科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以我覺得有點像是tednelson在1970年代初期時 , 他寫道: 「 你必須了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型的專家 , 沒有人想過 , 甚至在家裡有一家人 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你必須明白智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 先知新興科技是最好的方法 , 來確保我們在未來的新興科技是最好的方法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 用預測模式來計算安全的安全路線 , 用預測模式來計算安全道路的所有人的安全道路嗎 ? 但如果汽車可以分享資料 , 與他們相同 , 並且使用預測模式 , 來計算安全的路線 , 讓每個人在路上都沒有意外 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•福特:如果車子可以說話 , 意外可能會避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	咱們來面對它:駕駛很危險 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	我們不喜歡去思考 , 但事實上 , 宗教信仰和好運氣管弦在世界各地的現實中 , 我們都不喜歡去思考 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍發生在美國導致死亡率的75% , 造成死亡率的原因 , 不是因為死亡率和百分之七十五的原因 , 造成死亡率 , 造成死亡率 , 造成死亡率和百分之七十五 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以說清楚 , 但我記得我第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我是個年輕的駕駛在高速公路上 , 車子在我面前 , 我看到了火車在高速公路上 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢慢下來 , 我會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上腳踏車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙不會慢慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙正在停止 , 死停 , 停下來 , 死在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	僅僅是65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在布拉克上飛行 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我知道它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 車子也不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 車子也不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 車子也不會停下來 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道汽車停止了 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛體驗 , 讓車子互相交流 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是希望你們稍稍了解駕駛的經驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車子 , 穿著玻璃泡泡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受到你周圍的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是 , 在超human速度上 , 超human的速度 , 超human速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你必須指導你是兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這裡的所有人 , 都沒有設計這個任務 , 但人們會問你做的事 , 你想做的事 , 例如 , 你要做些什麼 , 第一件你要做的事 。
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛放在道路上 , 這是對的 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止看你在哪裡 , 看看你在哪裡 , 看看你在哪裡走路 , 不看你在哪裡 。

why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這麼做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我來看看這裡嗎 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一個很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上做些什麼 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾 , 我們錯過了 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會覺得錯誤或太遲了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數意外 , 駕駛說: 「 我沒有看到它 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但科技現在可以協助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 我們將能夠看到這些車子 , 不只有三輛車子 , 和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥眼的眼睛看 , 我們會看到這些車子 , 和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥眼的眼睛看 , 我們會看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們能看到在我們面前的車輛 , 看到車輛的速度 , 看得見得多快 , 或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個傢伙在0 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	實際上 , 沒有車子 , 不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維空間的物體 , 它有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們往路走路 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們在公開車道上發表 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要做理想的預測 , 對於車子的未來來說 , 很難做出理可預測 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在車子上 , 摩托車和摩托車司機時 , 摩托車和摩托車司機一小時下降了八十五英里 , 我知道你有這種經驗 , 沒有 「 只是從哪裡來 。 」
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個傢伙在路上一半小時內就在路上 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對嗎 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10、20、30英里 , 有人看過這個人 , 他在地圖上 , 很快地看到他在地圖上 , 很快地 , 有人看過那個傢伙 , 他在地圖上 , 很快地 , 他在地圖上 , 很快就會持續85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為車子會在他的耳朵中 , 比如說: 「 五分鐘、摩托車、摩托車 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以對汽車做出理想的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們該怎麼辦到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的角度來看 , 只要分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有一台攝影機和攝影機 , 我有很精準的點子 , 我有很精確的點子 , 我有很精確的點子 , 我有很精確的點子 , 我有很精確的點子 ,
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	用電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子 , 哪些車子 , 等等 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他車子一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以有一個精確的點子 , 和其他汽車的概念一樣 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩個車子分享資料 , 如果他們互相交談呢 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	教授和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬結果 , 例如:鋼鐵攝影機、gps , 和電腦模擬器 , 用電腦模擬器來做電腦模擬 , 當車輛分享gps時 , 我們已經把這個研究應用在電腦模擬中 , 例如:鋼鐵攝影機、gps , 和電腦模擬器 , 我們已經把這個研究應用在電腦模擬器上 , 同時 , 電腦模擬器現在正在進行電腦模擬測驗 , 甚至在車子裡 , 我們已經把這個研究放到電腦模擬中 , 甚至在車子裡 , 我們已經把這個研究放到電腦模擬中 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也將不同頻率的頻率傳播 , 機器人彼此溝通 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人互相交流時 , 它們會追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們會追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們會追蹤彼此的位置 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	現在我們把更多的機器人加入混合物中 , 我們會遇到一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你太多挑戰時 , 很難處理所有的包包 , 所以你必須優先考慮 , 要處理所有的包包 , 所以你必須優先考慮 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人汽車是追蹤預測軌跡的軌跡 , 你不用注意那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把這個傢伙看起來有點不好了 。
that guy could be a problem .	這傢伙可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新軌道 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他是怎麼走的 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而你知道駕駛你需要什麼駕駛才能避免 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做的是如何讓大家成為最好的 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼會說: 「 你需要脫離路嗎 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它依賴兩件事:一、汽車的能力 , 以及第二個駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有很棒的車子 , 但他們在電話或你知道 , 做些什麼 , 他們不可能會在最佳的位置上對緊急的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一系列的研究執行司機模式 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用一系列三台攝影機 , 我們能偵測到如果駕駛員在手機上 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測 , 車子 , 最好的位置 , 可以預測誰 , 車子是最好的位置 , 可以預測誰 , 車子是最好的位置 , 來計算安全的安全路徑 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術存在今天 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們所面臨的最大問題是我們自己的願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我覺得這是一個很讓人沮喪的概念 , 認為這是一個很讓人沮喪的概念 , 我們的車子會在海底下走路 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以被保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我看著你的車從外面看 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	假如我看你是多少 , 我並不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後說話 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位想像一下 , 如果你真的不希望你有一刻的青少年 , 那你就會死去 , 停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由分享我們的數據 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 咱們來看看你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprenhawkerpeterdiamandis談他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金 , 讓他能從中空中 , 加入大氣中 , 並且從中空中 , 再加上空氣 , 再加上大氣層 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談、空間、科技、宇宙 。

well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 唯一能體驗到地球的唯一方式是透過飛行、無限的飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿飛機 , 飛過最高 , 直到25秒鐘 。

medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療動畫家大衛•波林斯科目睹了三分鐘的刺激 , 顯示在一個細胞內的生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、技術、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	大衛•鮑林斯基y動畫了一個細胞 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插畫家 , 我從不同的觀點來看 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	從我長大後 , 真相和美麗在科學領域中表現出真相和美麗 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是很美好的事物 , 因為科學和數學幾乎像理想的青少年 , 一個科學家會想要約會的熱情和美麗 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是真實的表達方式 , 意思是 , 說他們是你能做的事 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	他們是很有力的 , 很不可思議 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨特的 , 有時通常很長時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你們現在可以從螢幕上看我 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美麗是常常被忽略在科學中的人 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	他們是用這種方式來描述美麗的事物 , 只要你了解語言和美麗的語言和美感 , 就會被表達出來 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看看數學 , 平方 , 如果你看數學 , 宇宙的原則 , 你可以看到生命必須從數字描述宇宙的角度來看 , 宇宙是非常困難的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導時 , 我想要找出一種方法來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用影像 , 透過使用影像 , 透過使用圖像 , 用圖像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用圖像 , 透過使用圖像 , 不必要的證據 , 來協助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用圖像 , 來協助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用圖像 , 來協助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用圖像 , 以便能了解真相和美麗 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生們通常會在環境中學習 , 被教導是很有真相和美麗的事物 , 但他們教學的主題是:真相和美麗並不總是有證據 。

and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我在哈佛大學的電話叫robertluehrvard的電話 , 他在哈佛大學 , 幾年前 , 我有一個電話 , 他問我 , 如果我的團隊和我有興趣 , 能真正改變醫學和科學教育是如何運作的 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	於是我們開始研究一個專案 , 讓學生可以了解更大的圖像 , 可以讓學生可以了解更大的圖像 , 可以讓學生可以了解更大的圖像 , 可以讓學生可以了解更大的圖片 , 可以讓學生可以了解更大的圖片 。

and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微生物的心臟是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微型machine , 它是世界上最有力的、精確的、精確的、精準的、精確的、精確的、精確的、精確的、精確的 , 由於胺基酸的基礎 。

and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想要做的是 , 我們想要做的是 , 把這些視覺化合成一個細胞生物學學生 , 把這些視覺放到腦中 , 讓這些學生們能夠找到真正的生物學學生 , 把這些視覺放在腦海裡 , 讓這些學生們能夠找到真正的生命 , 研究這些觀點 , 讓他們的心靈會被激發 , 這樣他們才能找到真正 , 生命的運作方式 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始觀察這些分子如何聚集在一起 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題有關 , 其中有一大堆的細胞 , 上面有一層薄膜 , 裡面有著外面的水面 , 它們會從細胞中發出訊息 , 在那裡 , 它們會吸收到外面的細胞 , 而它們會在外面的水面上發出訊息 , 而它們會從細胞中得到的訊息 , 它們會被送到外面 , 在那裡 , 牠們無法看見和感覺 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們有了這些資訊 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 讓它們改變它們的形狀 ,
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子分子運動 , 我們必須與哈佛科學家和資料庫的模型合作 , 找出它們如何移動 , 並找出它們如何移動 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	找出如何做到這一點 , 其實是很有用的 , 但不太有真理 , 讓大家知道 , 要怎麼做 , 才能預防病毒發生的狀況 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是 , 我們製作的第一部影片 , 它是一支三分鐘的閱讀器 , 是我們製作的這個影片的第一面 , 這是我們製作的第一個面向 , 它是一個持續發展的計畫 , 接下來要花五年的時間 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看看這個 , 看到這些小行行機器的路徑 , 他們稱之為基礎 , 用這些巨大的路徑來處理這些巨大的路徑 , 將這些巨大的路徑放在相對的路徑上 。
run the movie , please .	拍電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器在細胞內部的功能非常驚人 , 它們其實是生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器都能與彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	他們互相傳遞訊息 。

and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造出一部分 , 來自核子的分子 , 由分子閱讀基因組成的部分 。

in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在這些機器中 , 克里斯 , 真的很恐怖 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是fedex的傳送器 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做kinesin , 他推出了一堆新的製造蛋白質 , 包含了所有品牌新製造蛋白質 , 不管它是如何製造蛋白質 , 不管是用細胞 , 或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這些東西正在運作 , 目前 , 在每一百兆個細胞中 , 都有大約十萬個這種東西 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多瘋狂 , 你其實沒有做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當我回家想想看 , 我們的大腦有多強大 。

but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但真的很驚人 , 這些細胞 , 這些細胞 , 需要這些微生物 , 來了解這些細胞 , 需要他們做些什麼 。

becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布朗頓計劃在她的旅館上去年 , 看到國家 , 但當憂鬱症和她隔離時 , 她的經歷變成了美國無家可歸的年輕人 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會變革、社會改變、社會變革、社會改變、社會、社會改變、社會變革、社會變革、社會變革、社會變革
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪.布蘭頓:我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我知道如何做很多新的事物 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到如何做的事情之一就是變成隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我變成了無家可歸的人 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭職 , 決定要去旅行 , 決定要旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡非常困難 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	我在做這件事時 , 有許多事情 , 我想要感覺和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我把整個人生都活在一趟旅程中 , 我決定住在一個旅行的旅程中 , 我決定住在一個旅行的旅程中 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我拿著我的貓 , 我把我的貓帶走 , 開了車子 , 開了車子 , 開了車 , 開了一輛車 , 開了一輛車 , 開了一輛車 , 完全失敗了 , 發現了三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會平均生活在永久的結構上 , 甚至是一群人 , 甚至是一群人 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我失敗了 , 了解到他人能影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓他人能影響我們的現實 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我失敗了意識到無家可歸是態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	首先 , 住在火星是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在校園裡 , 常常出現 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但 , 憤怒和憂鬱 , 是我父親的死刑 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 , 我得要得到一份全職的工作 , 才能付出帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	最近的熱夏天夏天是非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	讓公園沒有很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 其實我非常熱衷 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓帶走了一輛開窗的窗戶 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗走進了白天照護
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能用員工時 , 我用員工的辦公室大樓和卡車停下來 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或我在公共場合的公共場所 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜晚的溫度 , 在華氏80度的溫度下降到華氏80度 , 讓它很難或不可能睡覺 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中發動 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我冰層的冰度上升了幾小時 , 而且它非常糟糕 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法負擔得起一個公寓 , 不能負擔得起一個公寓 , 或不能負擔得起公寓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕給他們放棄 , 所以我留在火車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱讓我太生病時 , 我用一塊垃圾桶 , 用一桶垃圾桶 , 用一桶和垃圾桶 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天天氣開始 , 溫度下降 , 溫度下降 , 溫度下降 , 溫度降低了 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一個全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停下來 , 所以我會避免注意到 , 被警察攔截 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺到我人生的控制 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時何地或怎麼發生 , 但我從一名無家可歸的藝術家和記者 , 到一個無家可歸的家人 , 和記者 , 把我的呼吸帶回來 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 。 我的智商 , 沒有改變 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的天賦、我的價值觀、我的價值觀 , 和我的價值觀 , 完全不一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我更深入憂鬱 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我送到一個無家可歸的醫療診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 , 我在三天內完成了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和憂鬱症一樣 , 像任何人一樣 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉或高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾位無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一位前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 。 為什麼你在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的家人都看不見我無家可歸 , 但我做了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	無家可歸的無家可歸 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給了我的憂鬱症 , 我記得我心想: 「 如果我殺了我自己 , 沒有人會注意 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友告訴我 , 很久以前 , 她聽說過西姆•俄羅斯 , 一個全國性的記者 , 一直在談論我 , 全國性的新聞報導 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一篇關於我父親的故事 , 在他死前的一年 , 在他死去之前 , 在他死去之前 , 他死去 , 是在tim的新書中 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	當時他正在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertste
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為它到達的地方 , 我是作家 , 或是我是個無家可歸的人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書 , 我找到了tim的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 然後我把我的文字排列 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	不久之後 , 我搬回去密度 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我住在一間飯店裡 , 與朋友一起吃飯 。
and i started writing again .	我開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	今年夏天 , 我是記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎勵 , 我住在我自己的公寓 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	成千上萬的人工作 , 生活在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續著侵犯罪犯 , 或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇見一個人 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何事情如果它有希望 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是在這裡 , 要成為那些無家可歸的女性 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是在這裡鼓勵你去鼓勵你去鼓勵你去鼓勵你去鼓勵你 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是他們生活在哪裡 , 或他們生活在哪裡 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我在華盛頓特區公園大廳工作 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是找到一種方式 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchaiviravaidya時 , 美國國會開始在1970年代 , 首先步:人口控制 。 這意味著很多法蘭克 , 非常有效的談談保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	伊維拉瓦迪亞:馬爾 , 泰國有更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	那時我年輕人40年前 , 國家很貧窮 , 許多人都住在貧困中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們沒有從一個福利計畫或貧窮降低的案例開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭的計畫開始 , 有一個非常成功的兒童健康活動 , 包含了非常成功的兒童健康活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人接受家庭計劃如果孩子沒有生存 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:到孩子 , 到母親 , 然後接著家庭規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是孩子的死亡率 , 你也需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在 , 讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	七個孩子在3.3%到3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 咱們來做吧 ! 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會吃藥 , 但我們需要醫生來治療藥物 。 」
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把問題當作一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和同性戀者 , 也是女性 , 做了一個很棒的工作 , 來解釋如何使用藥丸 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	這很棒 , 但它只佔了20%的國家 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們對其他80%的人說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定要做更多 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以 , 我們去了你看到的一般人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那黃色的黃色標誌裡 , 我希望他們還沒想過 , 因為有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	那時 , 我們比cocacocacocacocacocacola還大 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差異 , 他們選擇的人就是我們選擇的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	在社區中 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很擅長 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很擅長 , 他們很擅長 , 他們很擅長 , 他們很擅長 , 他們很擅長 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以供應藥丸和保險套 , 在全國各地的村落中 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們去了那些被視為解決方案的人 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	無論你在哪裡去找人 , 你會發現在泰國的販賣香蕉、螃蟹、販賣香蕉、販賣香蕉、螃蟹 , 還有避孕法 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 教堂非常強壯 , 和泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我是藍色的 , 不是黃色的 , 黃色的確保留著一碗水 , 讓家人的飲料和保險套用在藥品上 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片被送到整個國家 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	在村子裡的一些猴子也一樣做自己 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女性會說: 「 不奇我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	很幸運 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商業缺乏商業技能和取得信仰的人 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧型手機可能會感覺像朋友 , 但一個朋友 , 會給你一杯咖啡 , 一杯咖啡 , 一杯咖啡 , 在ted2013年 , 克萊納多•德莫斯•羅莫斯 , 一個朋友 , 給你一杯杯咖啡 , 用程式表達的方式來傳播 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個mini機器人 , 來自你的手機 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	舉手來說 , 你們當中有多少人有機器人在家裡 ?
not very many of you .	不是很多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好吧 , 實際上 , 那些手 , 如果你不包含房子裡有多少人有機器人在家裡 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在努力解決的問題 , 在我和其他20個街頭的角度 , 正是解決方案的原因 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要建造一個機器人 , 任何人都可以使用 , 無論你是八歲或八歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是非常困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 不只能負擔得起 , 而是要讓人們真正想要帶回家和孩子 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這種機器人不能是奇怪或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個機器人 , 用一種裝置你已經知道和愛你的iphone的機器人 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	利用iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造出一個機器人 , 可以創造出一個機器人 , 可以創造出一個機器人 , 可以創造出一個機器人 , 可以創造出一個機器人 , 可以創造出一個機器人 , 可以創造出一個機器人 , 可以創造一個機器人 , 可以在過去花費超過150美元 。

this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這讓你想要 , 讓你想要的 , 讓你想要的 , 讓你想要的 。

and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有一些你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它放在你的機器人上 , 並在真實生活中進行這個計畫 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有一些你很驕傲的事 , 你可以和其他人分享它 , 和世界上任何一個機器人一樣 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些wifi的機器人可以從彼此身上學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們非常專注在建造機器人上 , 每個人都可以訓練的原因是我們認為最具體的機器人是個人機械的 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人身上改變 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為如果你要在你的家裡有一個機器人 , 機器人應該是你自己的想像力 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你未來的個人機器人的樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們所知道的是 , 不是10億美金或大型人工機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	未來的個人機器人是現在的樣子 , 它會依賴小型、巨大的機器人 , 像是romo和創造力的人 。

author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和活動主義者和活動主義者會談話 , 當然 , 熱情在此談話中 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球性議題、愛、養育、故事、女人、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿拉伯爾所有人都說出了熱情的熱情 。
