there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我愛 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	真相是什麼 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個故事者 , 我想要傳達出一種比真相 , 更真實的事實 , 是我們共同的人類 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都很感興趣我 , 直到我最後寫他們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	肯定會說:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題 , 自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們周遭的神秘 , 所以我寫了有關巧合的力量 , 自然的魔法 , 魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去20年 , 我發表了幾本書 , 但在2006年 , 我剛剛出版了幾本書 , 當時我在2006年出版了幾本書 , 當時我在奧林匹克市旗中參加奧運會議 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為了名人 。 現在人們意識到我是很酷的 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我來告訴你們關於我四分鐘的信息 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧運會議員之一 , 開放式典禮的其中一位參加者 , 叫做我 , 說我被選為是旗幟之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我重複這個案例是錯誤的身分 , 因為我身為一個運動員 , 你能從運動員身上得到運動員 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	實際上 , 我甚至不確定我可以在台上游泳 , 甚至不確定我可以走進家裡 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑聲 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 唯一女性會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五個女性 , 代表五個大陸 , 還有三位奧林匹克王贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 天然 , 我要穿什麼 ?

they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得去贏 , 但有幸運的幸運 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一片雪 , 風力的一部分 , 風力的力量 , 可以判斷出種族或遊戲的力量 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的比訓練或幸運是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有懼怕和決心 , 才會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	一切都是熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	街頭和紅色海報者宣佈了奧林匹克的街頭 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活在這裡 , 不是總是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心臟是驅使我們決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我在書中所需要的:熱情心臟 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks、外國人、外國人、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外觀者、外
people like all of you in this room .	像在座的各位一樣 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	很有意思的傢伙 , 不是有趣的角色 。

in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在室內的綠色房間 , 我遇見了其他旗幟:三個運動員 , 和蘇菲亞洛倫 。

she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她很像一隻巨大的旗幟 , 把旗幟放在她的肩膀上 , 所以我的頭部在海岸的旗幟上 , 抓住旗幟的旗幟 。

a place where most men would love to be .	大部分的人會喜歡去的地方 。

my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我的丈夫被告知當我跟他說 , 雖然我告訴他 , 我們在私人身上做的事 , 通常只花不到四分鐘 , 但他不該怎麼做 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有了這些四個美好的消息 , 因為我不想忘記他們 , 年齡摧毀我的大腦細胞 。

so here's a tale of passion .	這是熱情的熱情 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 這個地方是一個監獄營 , 一個監獄營 , 位在剛果的監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上有80%的難民和女性和女孩們 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱之為 「 死亡營養 」 , 因為那些沒有殺死的人會死掉 , 或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 羅斯基地圖 , 她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵們被迫害她的丈夫被逮捕 , 被殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知如何 , 她會讓她的七個孩子活下來 , 幾個月後 , 她給出生嬰兒 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她切割了黏液 , 用她的頭髮來刺激 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她稱之為雙胞胎 , 用黑茶茶 , 因為她的牛奶無法保持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的牢房中傷害她 , 她抓住她並拒絕去除去 , 甚至當他們拿著槍枝時 , 她抓住她 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知如何 , 亞利桑那州的七十六個月後 , 美國人的心情 , 一名年輕美國人的心臟 , 亞利桑納州 , 亞利桑納州 , 她們現在生活和茁壯成長 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在swahili , 代表偉大的愛情 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我的書籍的主張是很強烈且熱情的女性 , 就像羅斯地圖一樣 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不會把它們放出來 , 不需要這樣做 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我看著周圍 , 看到它們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我和女性和女性一起工作 , 為女性和女性 。
i know them well .	我知道他們很好 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古老的日子 , 在世界各地 , 最後 , 在一個父權和保守派的家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	不想 , 五歲時 , 沒有人知道我的腦袋是怎麼回事的 , 所以沒有人知道我的腦袋是怎麼回事 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 有一個高價格 , 來付出我的自由 , 去找尋求助我的自由 , 去找尋求助我的自由 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興 , 因為每次我收到的垃圾桶 , 我就得到了兩種 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	一旦 , 當我女兒保羅拉在她的二十歲時 , 她告訴我 , 女性主義是約會的 , 我應該搬進去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有了不可思議的抗議 , 女性主義是約會嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 像我的女兒和今天的女性 , 像我的女兒和所有人 , 但不是在世界上大部分的姊妹 , 仍然被迫使勞動力勞動力勞動力勞動力 , 她們有孩子 , 不希望或無法被迫害 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們沒有控制自己的身體或生命 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育、沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、被逮捕 , 有時被殺害 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	現今大部分西方年輕女性主義者是個侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從來沒有性別 , 但讓我保證 , 女性主義從來沒有性別 , 但我讓我保證你從來不會阻止我 , 女性主義從來不會阻止我 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義不是死 , 也不是死 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經演化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 為上帝的命運 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為 「 愛 」 、 「 愛 」 、 「 愛 」 、 「 愛 」 、 「 不 」 、 「 不論 」 的意思 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這裡還有另一個關於熱情的熱情 , 這是個悲傷 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	在孟加拉的一個村落裡 , 一個小女人的診所 。
the year is 2005 .	一年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙齒牙醫師 , 在她的三週期間 , 在她的三週期間 , 一位年輕的牙醫醫生 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備乾淨牙齒 , 但當她發現 , 醫生沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面 , 有一群婦女在等待幾小時被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人是非常痛苦的 , 因為她有幾種旋轉的動作 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到 , 唯一解決方法是要推出最好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她從來沒有這麼做 , 她從來沒有做過這件事 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適合的儀器 , 但幸運的是她已經帶了一些鼻子 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇敢和熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她是一位禱告者 , 和她一起進行手術 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 受傷的病人吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生棉花了很多牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 她的第一個病人在等待她的丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來像是水龍 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它是如此 , 你甚至無法看見眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫 , 威脅要殺死美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮在她所做過的情況中感到害怕 , 但後來翻譯員解釋病人的狀況和手術沒有關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	隔天之前 , 她丈夫打敗她 , 因為她沒有家在準備晚餐給他 。
millions of women live like this today .	數百萬的女性生活在今天 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性在世界上三分之三的勞動力中 , 他們不到百分之三十的勞動力 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水比男性一樣 , 若他們有薪水 , 他們就很容易被剝削、暴力和虐待 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是賦予女性教育、工作 , 能控制自己的收入、自我的能力 , 以及自己的財產權利 , 能控制自己的收入、社會 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果女性有權力 , 她的孩子和家人就會變得更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家就會成功 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai在肯亞的村落 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女談話 , 說:土地是綠色的 , 因為他們砍伐樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓女性植物新的樹木和水 , 以下降落 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五或六年之內 , 他們有森林 , 土壤被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最貧窮的最貧窮和最貧窮最貧窮最貧窮最貧窮最貧窮最貧窮最貧窮最最窮的人
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但顯然的事實是忽略政府和慈善事業 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一塊錢給男性的計畫 , 二十美元給男性的程式 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們能改變一切 , 不只是科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以保證各位 , 女性一起合作 , 和平與繁榮 , 能夠承諾 , 能夠承諾 , 和平和平和平 , 能夠承諾 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的戰爭中 , 大部分的職場都是公民 , 主要是女性和孩子 , 主要是女性和孩子 , 主要是女性和孩子 , 主要是女性和孩子 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑遍世界 , 看看我們所擁有的一切 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	它是否能夠合理參與現有的世界秩序 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個世界 , 生活的品質和生活品質 , 不僅是為了榮幸而已 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月 , 我在柏克萊圖書館看到了一個展覽 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有博物館或ghraib監獄 , 沒有任何博物館或ghraib監獄 , 因為這個主題是阿布•普勒斯博物館 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們是巨大的畫作和虐待的力量 , 在廣大的畫作中 , 被暴露在巨大的痛苦中 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法把這些影像從我的腦中或我的心臟跳出來 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我害怕大部分的力量是權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及權力濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則改變了所有時間 , 但他們總是有益處 , 在這個案例中 , 這種案例中 , 效果不在經濟上 , 非常有效 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	以下降到最底層的底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女性和孩子 , 尤其是窮人 , 尤其是窮人 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即便是最多的女性還是小孩 , 都可以虐待女性或小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我在許多性別、收入、種族、種族和課堂上都有能力 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間在我們的文明中創造根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但為了真正的改變 , 我們需要女性的能源來管理世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要針對女性權力的女性權力 , 我們需要培養女性的女性權力 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我指的是年輕人的心智 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人無希望 ; 我們必須等待他們死掉 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很喜歡有蘇菲亞洛琳長腿和腿部的長腿和腿部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 為了選擇 , 我會有一個選擇 , 我會和羅斯•馬利•瑪麗•瑪麗•瑪麗•瑪麗•瑪麗•瑪麗•瑪麗•瑪麗•瑪麗•瑪麗•瑪麗•瑪麗•瑪麗 , 媽媽 , 珍妮 ,
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變得好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不好 , 但要讓它好好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 它可能 。 看看這個房間所有的知識、能源、科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們走進我們的口袋裡 , 打開我們的口味 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 每一天 , 在城市的大小 , 建築師卡羅•史蒂爾討論了一座城市的大小 , 一座城市的大小 , 建築師卡羅•史提夫說 , 建築師卡羅•史提夫說 , 現代世界有多麼的不可思議 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳•史蒂爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們時代最棒的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	然而 , 一個很少被問到的問題 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們很神奇地從某處走進一間餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你想到每一天 , 城市都要被運輸、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、買賣、煮飯、吃掉 , 不論你想到哪裡 , 都要被運輸、買賣、買賣、買賣、煮飯、吃掉 , 和它很不一樣 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在自然世界中 , 如我們所知 , 我們的生活就像是地球上最自然的事物 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們必須吃 , 我們其實依賴自然世界 , 為我們的古老祖先 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們進入城市 , 自然世界變得更加深刻 , 如同我所在巴西的地景 , 把我們帶進城市裡 , 自然世界被轉變成了很棒的地景 , 像是我在巴西的土地景 , 來餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的景觀 , 但少數人會看到他們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的地景並不只是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著更多人搬進城市裡 , 我們吃肉 , 只剩下三分之一的穀物在吃肉 , 所以 , 現今世界上的三分之一的穀物被餵食肉 , 而不是人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	若有三倍以來餵飽人類 , 那就不是非常有效率的餵食方式 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個嚴重的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計人口數量將會住在城市中 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	它也估計 , 兩倍的肉類和diry消耗量都很高 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉和城市主義都在手上 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會提出一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	六十億個飢餓的卡尼佛 , 到2050年 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個很大的問題 , 如果我們帶著我們 , 真的是很不可思議的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有900萬英畝的雨林 , 造成新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同樣的時間 , 我們失去了一份相當量的保存方式 , 可以讓珊瑚化和消耗 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們對化石燃料也很渴望 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	需要大約10卡路里 , 來製造出我們消費的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有食物在大成本上 , 我們並不值得它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國有一半的食物被丟棄了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	最後 , 在這段漫長的過程中 , 我們還沒辦法餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們有十億人是肥胖者 , 數十億人是肥胖 。
none of it makes very much sense .	沒有什麼是很合理的 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為百分之八十的全球貿易已經被五個跨國公司所控制 , 只是五個跨國公司 , 這是一張圖片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們搬進城市時 , 世界也會擁抱西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 它是一個永續飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們是怎麼辦到的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	嗯 , 要回答一個更簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 剛剛剛剛剛剛提到的一萬年前 , 叫做 「 肥皂蛋糕 」 的開始 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是有形狀的 。
and it was also fertile .	這也是肥料 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前 , 這兩種非凡的發明、農業和城市主義 , 發生在同一個地方 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市是互相的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為我們古老的祖先第一次製造出食物來源 , 足以支撐永久的環境 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些居民的樣子 , 我們看到他們是很合理的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	牠們被大型的土地和中央食物分配中心提供中心食物分配中心
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是天賦的寺廟 , 把穀物取代 , 把穀物帶回來 , 把穀物給上帝 , 再把穀物給上帝 , 不再吃回來 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 所有這些城市的靈性和實體生活都是由穀物和穀物所組成的 , 包含了它們 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老城市都一樣 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有這些都很小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	很有名的 , 羅馬有大約一百萬個公民 , 羅馬有一百萬個公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 這種城市如何像這樣的城市 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古代食物哩 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬接近了海 , 讓它可以從遠遠遠遠的地方 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代世界中唯一的方法 , 因為它很難運輸食物 , 路上是很困難的 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然很快 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬效應的戰爭 , 像是卡路和埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及只能把他們抓住的地方 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可能會說 , 擴張的擴張是很長的 , 擴張的擴張是很長的 , 擴張到軍事的擴張 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實:羅馬 , 其實我很喜歡這個事實:羅馬其實是從倫敦到倫敦的一個階段 。 我認為這是很棒的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬形狀它的形狀 , 以它的形狀為基礎 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看倫敦的地圖的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的地圖是從十七世紀開始的地圖的地圖 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 黃金市場則是城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從他們到便宜的道路 , 主要市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看這個名字的名字 , 布雷德街 , 你可以在300年前看到這條路線 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚類也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚類也是一樣的 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 很有名的是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這是很不尋常的 , 當你想到它的時候 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	每個人都穿著手機 , 看起來像是磚塊 , 像磚塊一樣 , 還在港口上移動 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是另一個關於食物的城市:一旦它根入城市裡 , 它們很少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	當然 , 動物可以走進城市裡 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦的肉來自西北部、蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以 , 它開始了 , 在那裡 , 北邊的冰川 , 在那裡 , 那裡有著名的肉市場 , 位在北邊 , 這是為什麼smithfield , 倫敦非常有名的肉市場 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	波特里亞是來自東加利亞的東部 , 東北方 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像天氣女性 , 這樣做 , 鳥兒們來到他們的腳邊 , 用小小的蠟燭來拍照 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	接著 , 當他們抵達東方的東方便宜時 , 他們被賣出來了 , 這就是為什麼它被稱為大屠殺 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看在工業時代的地圖 , 你能從工業時代取得食物 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何塑造食物的 , 透過閱讀街道的名字 , 給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五 , 一個星期五的街道 , 就是你去買你的魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你必須想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間只是食物被買賣的唯一地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看在1830年的圖片 , 你可以看到 , 在1830年時 , 你可以看到它會非常困難地住在城市裡 , 像這樣 , 不清楚你的食物從哪裡來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期日的午餐 , 可能是在你的窗戶外面 , 大約三天前就在你的窗戶外面 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這很明顯是有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西方的影像 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 最早的訓練乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被視為悲傷和心智 , 在國家的某個地方 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們會進入城市 ,
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 要開始發展城市 , 任何地方 , 都可以做得很大 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	城市以前被地理所被地理所限制 , 他們習慣要把食物帶到非常困難的實體 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 他們都被從地理中解放 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見的 , 在火車的地圖上 , 大約九十年後 , 在火星的地圖上 , 很容易餵飽動物 , 以此類推 , 很容易餵飽動物 , 以此類推 , 很容易餵飽動物 , 以此類推 , 很容易餵飽動物 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然那只是一開始 , 火車結束後 , 火車就結束了 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是整個城市與大自然的聯繫 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是一種城市 , 可以避免氣味 , 沒有人會夢想在這樣的地景上走進去 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們的食物是他們的車子 , 一週的購物中心 , 來回去買一周的購物物品 , 並想在地球上做些什麼 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這真的是我們的關係 , 食物和城市 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有食物被用來成為中心 , 城市的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它曾經是社交活動 , 買賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前烹煮了 , 只是加上水 , 或一些蛋糕 , 或一些蛋糕 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看它是否好吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是在一堆紙上貼上標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不相信它 。 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不相信它 , 我們害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是評估它 , 我們將它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的最棒諷刺之一就是他們承諾要讓更容易變得更困難 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	讓它可以建造城市 , 任何地方 , 都能在我們和大自然中建立起城市 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	同時他們也讓我們依賴系統 , 只能提供我們所見 , 不穩定的系統 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	所以 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯會問自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	它是一系列獨立的餐廳 , 每人都很熟悉 , 有一天從另一個地方 , 每個人都很熟悉 , 從一個人的角度 , 到處都是種植蔬菜 , 在他們後花園的餐廳裡 , 再生長蔬菜 , 再加上餐具 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為你可以說食物是烏托邦的基本原則 , 即使從來沒有這樣做 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	還有另一個非常有名的烏托邦 「 烏托邦 」 、 「 烏托邦 」 、 「 烏托邦 」 、 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的點子:一系列獨立的城市 , 單獨的城市 , 加入了獨立的城市 , 加入了獨立的城市 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以被說是他的視野的原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造了 , 但沒有用這種視覺去做 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這些烏托邦的想法是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦是湯瑪斯•摩爾使用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它有來自希臘的高峰 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以代表一個好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的 , 不可思議的 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 來思考人類的重大問題 , 讓它不用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我有了另一個替代方案 , 例如: 「 西班牙語 」 、 「 西班牙語 」 、 「 西班牙語 」 、 「 芝加利亞 」 、 「 西班牙語 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西比亞 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個塑造世界不同的角度 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們能用食物來塑造世界不同的角度 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們要這麼做 , 西雅圖像什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 只是在狗的臉上 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	不管怎樣 , 這是食物在生活的中心 , 家庭生活的中心 , 家庭生活的中心 , 被慶祝 , 享受 , 人們花時間 。
this is where food should be in our society .	食物應該在我們的社會裡 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不能像這樣 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順帶一提 , 這些都是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 想到食物 , 誰會想到食物 , 誰會想到食物 , 誰會想到食物 , 誰會想到食物 , 誰會想到食物 , 誰會想到食物呢 ?
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這些人 , 我們就無法像這樣 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我真的選了這個 , 因為它是男人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網路、市場 , 食物正在成長的地方 。
it's common . it's fresh .	它很常見 , 很常見 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	這是城市的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為 , 沒有這種地方 , 你不能有這種地方 , 食物也就是地景的一部分 , 而不是僅僅是地景的一部分 , 而不是單純的零件商品 。
cows with a view .	擁抱著觀點 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽的山脈 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上就是把整合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近參加的社區計劃 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是溫室 , 孩子們被告知食物和種植的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一個叫做凱文的植物 , 或它是植物屬於一個叫做凱文的孩子 , 或者它是植物屬於一個叫做kevin的孩子 , 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	總之 , 這些計畫在試圖與大自然極其重要 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 烏托邦對我來說是個看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 在小小的口袋裡 , 每個地方都有一些口袋 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	技巧是要加入它們 , 用食物作為一種看待方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們會停止看到城市 , 像這樣 , 大型的城市 , 大型的城市 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們視為是有機架構的一部分 , 它們是有機架構的 , 不可避免地 , 有機架構造 , 它們是無可避免的 , 有機架構造 , 它們是無可避免的 , 其中一部分是有機架構 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這不是很棒的圖像 , 因為我們需要不要再把食物做成 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要思考更多關於永生性 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖像剛剛提到我們要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	它是一種重新思考食物形塑我們的生活方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像是650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	這是亞伯羅•洛倫澤蒂的 「 政府的優秀政府 」 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	它是城市和國家之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息很明顯 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市在國外看 , 國家就會看到城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	今天我想要我們來問 , 如果他畫這張圖片 , 阿布羅•洛倫澤蒂的畫畫呢 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今日的政府看起來會怎樣 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個急迫的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須開始回答的 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們是吃的 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們必須意識到 , 世界也是我們吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採取這個想法 , 我們可以用食物作為一個非常強大的工具來塑造世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	幾週後 , 卡爾斯•阿姆斯壯在21世紀的信仰中找到了黃金法則 , 可以讓世界的信仰轉換成黃金規則 。

karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenmstrong:我們來保證黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我變得很沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我變得很沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我變得很沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我已經變得很沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我變得很沮喪 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都演化出自己的版本 , 叫做黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時候它會出現在正面的版本中: 「 總是對待你自己的人 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面版本: 「 別對其他人做你不喜歡他們做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你的心臟 , 發現它是什麼 , 讓你痛苦 , 並且拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 在任何情況下 , 都會造成疼痛 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調了同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 而是因為它是好的 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們把黃金法律寫成 「 日常生活 」 、 「 日常 」 、 「 日常生活 」 、 「 所有日子 」 時 , 不只會在你面臨的人生中 , 不斷地踏上你的生活 , 然後再回到一個生活中 , 和遺忘的人生中 , 最後 , 再回到一個生活中 , 和遺忘的人生中 , 最後 , 再回到一個生活中 , 和遺忘的人生中 , 最後 , 再回到一個生活中 , 再加上一輩子 , 再加上一輩子 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它將你帶到一個被稱為上帝、nirvana、nirvana、rama、nirvana 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	在我們所知的事物中 , 我們所知的事物就存在了 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你永遠不會知道太多時間 , 這才是宗教生活的中心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些奇妙的例外 , 通常宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 , 宗教領袖團聚在一起 ,
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不想同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到當我在說話時 , 人們常常會被認為是對的 , 因為人們常常想對抗 。

because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們把我帶到21世紀 , 讓我能從我的書線研究中帶領我到21世紀 , 讓我能夠更廣泛的聽見 , 讓我能從我的書線中學習並帶領我 。

if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	若我們不能管理全球的管理 , 以致於我們能把所有人、任何人 , 無論如何 , 無論他們是誰 , 他們可能是誰 , 他們可能是誰 , 他們可能是誰 , 儘管我們對待所有人 , 無論如何 , 他們都很重要 , 我懷疑我們能在未來的世代下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們時間的任務之一是建立一個全球社會 , 如我所說 , 人們可以與平共享 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而宗教應該要做主要的貢獻 , 而不是被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 這不僅僅是宗教相信黃金法則的人 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種想像性的同理心 , 把自己放到另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 對我來說 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	不論你在哪裡 , 或我們能回到拉比希拉比希爾 , 最古老的猶太教徒 , 拉比希爾 , 一個法律 , 說: 「 這對你的鄰居有很大的影響 。 」 說: 「 這對你的鄰居感到害怕 。

and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	拉比和早期的父親教堂 , 教會說任何詮釋的文字 , 都是違法的 。

religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教學 , 這樣我們就錯了 , 聚焦在信仰的教學上 。

and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥類管理會把自己帶走到最好的巴尼斯海岸邊 , 停止很久 , 直到我們剛剛剛剛提到的聖殿堂 , 停留在26英尺深的海岸邊 , 直到我們剛剛剛剛提到的 , 一邊有巴尼斯•納瓦納 , 我們已經剛剛提到 , 看到了一陣子 , 一路直到三十五英尺長的海岸 , 直到我們剛剛剛剛提到的 , 四個河流 , 一直在26英尺深的海岸上 , 看到了一陣子 , 停止夠久 , 直到我們剛剛剛剛提到的 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們就不需要擔心重力 , 因為我們飛行 , 我們不需要擔心重力 , 在這一刻 , 這張圖能被指引在某個時刻 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 這並不意外 , 要模仿這個建築 。

as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著畫板時 , 我們看到他正在努力的地圖 , 畫板的地圖 , 看到他正在努力的地圖 , 紅線延伸到所有洞穴的地圖 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 我們就得以閱讀這些圖案 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院學院的學生們設計了一種自我組裝的概念 , 不是建造東西 , 我們能創造材料 , 建造出一種自我組裝的模型 , 可以創造出自己 , 以自我組裝的構造方式 , 以自我組合的方式來建造 , 像這樣 , 我們能創造出一股巨大的架構 , 以自我組裝的構造方式 , 以自我組合的方式來建造 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	太陽能 , 可以讓自己做些什麼嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想給各位看我們製作東西的方式 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快的 , 我們的建築物和機器會自我組合 , 複製並修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要向各位展示我所相信的現代製造 , 和一些自然系統的運作方式相比 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在現有的技術上 , 我們有天花板 , 花了兩半年的時間 , 50萬到一百萬個部分 , 非常複雜、新的、令人興奮的科技 , 像是鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有很興奮的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年內 , 大約250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你觀察自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型 , 可以複製在大約一小時內 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們自然系統中的複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 比任何我們能建造的更有效率 , 更有效率 , 比任何我們能建造的更有效率 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們比能源更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們很難犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然系統有很有趣 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能把它轉化為我們的建設環境 , 那還有一些令人興奮的潛力 , 以我們建造的方式 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中做出自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有的複雜性 , 我們需要解碼所有我們所想要建造的建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼到簡單的序列 , 基本上就是我們建築物的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要編寫程式的部分 , 可以採取那個序列 , 用它來摺疊或修復 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量 , 讓它能夠從程式中解開 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型錯誤的反射線來保證我們成功地建立了我們所想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些我同事和我在麻省理工學院的工作 , 來達成這個自我組合的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	首先是麥克魯特和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些計劃是大規模可重複的機器人 , 十二公尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們被用機械電裝置、感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你將這個序列轉為120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每一個單位都將它傳送給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是聰明的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師在這個計畫上做這個計畫 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為這真的很可怕嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 數以千計的花費 , 數以千計的花費 , 讓這八英呎的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們能否真的把這些機械化成每一個部分 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 , 或熱情地嘗試修復程式 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 試圖實際計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它基本上是計算的數位邏輯 , 直接進入你的部分 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是一個nandgate 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有兩個輸入的鐵路 , 你有兩個輸入鐵 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是使用者的輸入 , 如你建造你的磚塊 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一個是從前所未見的磚塊 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你一個輸入3d空間 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要磚塊上做些什麼 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算了它在做什麼 , 你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 或下降 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以左手邊 , 1 , 1 , 1 , 1 , 1 , 輸入 , 輸入1.1 , 輸入等於0輸入 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0.0是1個輸入 , 輸入是1的輸入 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的資訊都被建構出來了 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我複製 , 因為你的結構包含了藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被嵌入了 , 告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有一些東西可以爬上去 , 閱讀它 , 並且可以從一個人身上學習 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接被嵌入 , 沒有外外的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	最後一個項目 , 我會展示的例子是 「 偏見鏈 」 , 它可能是最令人興奮的例子 , 是我們目前擁有的自我組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要重組和系統 , 讓它完全被動系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一堆元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都是完全相同的 , 它們偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每個鏈 , 或左邊 , 都想要轉右或左邊 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈 , 你基本上就是編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你要告訴每個單位 , 如果它應該轉右或左邊 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以 , 當你搖晃鏈 , 就會摺疊成任何你在這個案例中所做的事 , 或在這個案例中 , 兩個方塊組成一個旋律 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以你可以基本上設計任何三維空間的形狀或維度 , 把它放在這個鏈上完全被動化 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	這告訴我們什麼呢 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 它告訴我們 , 我們的建築物、機器 , 能自我組合、複製、複製、修復身體結構、建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部分中有新的可程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從你有新的可能性來計算 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是很棒的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以 , 這很讓人興奮 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為這些計畫我已經展示給一個新的自我組裝的世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們登陸月球 , 我們已經到達地球上最深的一刻 , 去探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索者
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、生物多樣性、探索、生物多樣性、探索、微生物學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:左邊要探究什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去拜訪了布萊斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康辛 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我很榮幸 , 十二十世紀的探險家 , 羅莉•查普曼•查普曼 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在美國自然歷史博物館中 , 大自然歷史的博物館長大了一系列的展覽 , 來到未知的區域 , 如今 , 在美國博物館 。
he was quite a figure .	他是非常的名字 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來 , 他就說 , 印度娜瓊斯特的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在華盛頓特區時 , 我給了一群中間的學校學生 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡要告訴各位 , 如果這裡有更令人難以置信的注意力 , 它會試著把注意力集合成千上萬12歲的孩童 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在課程結束時 , 他們問了一些問題 , 但有一件事我很困惑 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們要去哪裡 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為有許多人在地球上最深層的探索 , 要去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到明顯的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但那是真的嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	我們是否在地球上探索左邊的重要性嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我覺得回到我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家 , 馬丁斯•貝伊斯 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以beijerinck發現了菸草疾病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是 , 他把感染的汁液從菸草植物中拿出來 , 他把感染的汁液從菸草植物上 , 讓它更小的濾水 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他接觸到這個點子 , 知道細菌的存在 , 直到他所知細菌的生命中 , 最小的形式就存在了 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他提出了一個名字 , 名字是他的謎團 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在未知的病毒中 , 維魯士很快地把這個全新的世界帶給我們 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒將基因資訊傳遞到地球上 , 比其它生命組成的基因信息還要多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 有著很大的實際應用 , 例如 , 我們現在知道的 , 由人類普羅馬病毒病毒所造成的 , 很顯然有很大的實際應用 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	貝蒂克的發現 , 這並不是發生在500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百年前 , 維魯士發現病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有自動飛行器 , 但是我們沒有意識到地球上所有基因資訊的形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些奇妙的工具 , 讓我們能夠從特定的物種中尋找獨特的基因體 , 讓我們去探索那些未知的世界 , 像是深層的微生物 , 來記錄所有基因組的基因組 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以應用這些技術從土壤到皮膚和所有東西 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在正在進行一個規定的基礎 , 來找出造成爆發爆發的疫情 , 無法讓它們發生 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓大家了解這個作品如何運作 , 想像一下 , 想像一下 , 我們從每個人身上 , 想像一下 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常常去尋找呼吸器的病毒 , 像是流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先 , 我們會看到的是巨大的基因資訊 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究基因信息 , 我們會看到許多人的基因信息 , 大部分是來自於你鼻子裡完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了非常令人驚訝的事 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始觀察這些資訊時 , 我們會看到大約20%的基因信息 , 不論是在沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌之間的基因信息 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於小組我們實際上研究這些數據 , 我們當中有些人已經開始稱之為 「 資訊生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是我們以前所見過的 , 它是一種在我們自己的基因信息中所見過的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為20%的基因信息是生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 大約有40%或50%的基因信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的信息是黑暗物質無法被分類或配合我們所見過的東西 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	首先我們認為也許這是人工 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深密的工具是相對的 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得更精確 , 我們決定了這些資訊是生命的一種形式 , 或者至少有些是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然假設解釋了生物暗物質的存在性存在於其它的生命中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 有一種非常令人興奮的可能性存在:埋藏在這個生命中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 存在著生命的存在 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索這些弦 , 像是北京 , 基本上改變我們對生物學的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許會讓我們能夠辨識出我們對癌症的新工具 , 或找出癌症的原因 , 來找出癌症的原因 , 或找出我們所熟悉的新工具 , 或在分子生物學中找到一種新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興告訴各位 , 在史丹佛大學和加州史丹福大學的同事 , 我們目前正在進行一項探索生物暗物質 , 來探索生物暗物質存在於生命的新形式 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百年前 , 人們不知病毒 , 生命的形式 , 是我們地球上最大的基因信息 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會馬上發現 , 我們可能完全不了解新生命的新階段 , 其實是對我們的鼻子 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	真的 , 我們可能已經發現了所有大陸的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	伊斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康辛 , 他對下一代的年輕女孩提供了重要的課程 , 像是那位年輕女孩 , 伊斯康斯康斯康辛 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們把這句話說出來 , 就會像這樣:不假設我們現在所認為的 , 就是這個故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	除非你選擇去探索的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	不知我們周圍的周圍 , 都等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	法律科學家大衛•迪佛斯奇博士提出了理論物理 , 他說 , 要承認我們有問題 , 要承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、科學、科技 , 宇宙 , 宇宙 , 一切 , 科學 , 科技 , 宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛•迪佛斯在宇宙中 , 我們在宇宙中 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出去 , 說出令人意外的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著做這件事 , 但我想要從兩件事開始 , 大家都知道的 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 實際上 , 大部分紀錄歷史都已經被知道了 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或環境 , 不管我們在哪裡 , 都能維持我們的演化或創造力 , 尤其是我們的未來生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有一個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	而在太空船內 , 宇宙是無所不在的 , 宇宙是充滿敵意的 , 而我們的內部 , 我們都仰賴了 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們把太空船除去 , 我們就沒辦法去了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家都知道 , 人類歷史上的人類歷史 , 人類史上沒有 , 其實 , 人類歷史的存在 , 其實是不存在的 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如史蒂芬•霍金所說的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球 , 在一個典型的星球中 , 在一個典型的星球上 , 在一個典型的星球上 , 一個典型的星球 , 只是一個典型的銀河系 , 一個典型的星球 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家知道的意思是 , 我們在一個典型的狀態 , 第二個是說 , 我們在一個典型的狀態 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你把這兩者當作是深刻的真相 , 然後他們似乎會互相衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這不會阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	第二個問題是:典型的 。 嗯 , 我們看一下 , 一個典型的空間 , 嗯 , 我們看到一座牆 , 一個典型的空氣 , 我們看到一座牆 , 一個典型的空間 。 嗯 , 我們看到一座牆 , 一個典型的空間 。 嗯 , 我們看到一座牆 , 一個典型的空間 。 嗯 , 我們看到一座牆 , 一個典型的空間 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只能看到太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星在銀河系中 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	在宇宙中 , 大部分地方在宇宙中 , 幾乎沒有任何銀河系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再進一步 , 看看 , 回到星系 , 再來看看 , 是的 , 有一個巨大的銀河系 , 在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	在這個時候 , 我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然在宇宙中最常見的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你必須有一千次的空間 , 到達一個典型的地方 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	這看起來是什麼樣子呢 ?
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中的典型空間是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 非常高解析度的虛擬實境空間 , 用了高解析度的虛擬實境空間 , 來分析虛擬實境的空間 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以我們能看到它嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不完全是黑暗的 , 完全是黑暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它很黑暗 , 如果你要看著最近的星星 , 你仍然無法看見 , 甚至是一顆星球 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙的多大和黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管如此明亮 , 超新星是如此聰明的 , 所以 , 很明顯的 , 它會殺死你在幾光年內完成的事件 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從太空中 , 遠遠遠離你看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	同時也非常寒冷 , 不到三度 , 絕對是零 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它很空氣 , 空氣比地球上最高的空氣有一百萬倍 。 所以 , 這種特殊的地方是來自這個地方的 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的運作方式 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們可以有燈光嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在 , 我們如何知道一個環境是如此遙遠的 , 外星人 , 和外星人一樣 , 我們怎麼知道 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球的環境 , 我們的形式 , 是創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	這意味著什麼呢 ? 嗯 , 遠遠遠遠遠遠超過我們剛剛從這裡的一顆望遠鏡 , 你可以看到它看起來像星星一樣 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們被稱為 「 四軸 」 , 意思是 「 四軸 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著 , 看起來像星星一樣 , 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是數十億年前 , 數十億年前 , 數十億年前 , 星系的黑洞 , 形成了巨大的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場會引力爆炸的能量 , 一些重力崩潰的能量 , 其中一些物質 , 重力崩潰的能量 , 甚至是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學 , 不像物理的物理一樣 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法存活下來 , 當嘗試描述它所在的狀態時 , 語言破壞了 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	它會有點像是經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在一瞬間 , 數百萬年來 , 一個超新星爆炸 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 在宇宙的幾十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一邊 , 有些化學物件可以準確地描述、模型、預測 , 並且預測 , 解釋一下 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 有些化學可以準確地描述和預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 解釋一下 , 在宇宙的其他地方 , 有些化學可以準確地描述、模型、預測 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個體體系統 , 大腦 , 包含一個非常精確的模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是一個超級的圖像 , 同時也包含了同樣的數學關係和相同的數學關係和相同的數學關係 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識的知識 。 如果你不夠驚人 , 不夠精確 , 不夠精確 , 不夠精確 , 不夠精確的知識 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理學的物理有特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那些物理物體物品 , 不像彼此相同的數學和蛋糕結構 , 讓它更加快速地運作 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是化學的化量 , 化學的化量是不同的 。 化學的化量是不同的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構和內部的結構與其它的存在 , 不論是物理世界中的其他地方 , 其實是物理世界的一部分 , 實際上 , 物理世界的結構和其他地方 , 其實是物理世界的一部分 , 不論是哪個地方 , 都沒有其他地方 , 在宇宙中 , 它的結構和內部的結構和其他地方都存在 , 而非其他地方 , 在宇宙中 , 它的結構和內部的結構和其他地方都存在 , 實際上 , 物理世界的結構和結果 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼太陽系和我們的環境 , 我們如何與宇宙的相互作用 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬•霍金所說的 , 是真的 , 但這是錯的 。 這是真正的 , 但這是錯的 。 只有三件事 , 就是我們所擁有的 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有奇蹟 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個很重要 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的計算 , 計算的速度是資訊處理計算 , 計算的速度是計算的 , 計算需要電腦沒有任何東西的知識 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體影響我們所記錄的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 更不容易理解 , 但就算是證據 , 也是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境是有證據的 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們會開始進行測試 , 說 , 牛頓的重力約300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但證據顯示我們過去數十億年以後一直在地球上數十億年的證據 , 並且將持續下降 , 數十億年以後 , 仍然會繼續繼續下降 , 以至於所有其他科學都一樣 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	如我們所知 , 證據證明所有科學的所有科學都只是為了我們所知的 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置是充滿證據的 , 同時也很重要和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在二氧化碳中 , 最低的可能供應是最低的可能供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如同我所說的 , 它是空氣的 , 它是冷的 ; 它是冷的 ; 它是冷的 ; 它是冷的 ; 它是冷的 ; 它是冷藏的 。
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一種錯誤觀念 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個立方體在內部空間 , 和我們的家鄉 , 太陽系的大小 , 相同的尺寸是人類標準 , 但那仍然意味著它包含了超過百萬噸的重要性 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足夠的說 , 一個自動駕駛的太空站 , 在那裡 , 有一群科學家被投入 , 創造出一種開放式的知識 , 以此類推 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 遠遠超越科技甚至能把氫氣混合成其他元素和其他元素 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個不可思議的宇宙中 , 如果沒有被物理定律所發生的一切 , 那麼我們可以避免我們從事的事物中 , 什麼可能阻止我們去做它呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是知識 , 不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動地使用能源供應 , 因為通訊會變成核融合反應爐和證據 。
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 再說一次 , 人類的感知是很明顯的 。 但你要做的是用望遠鏡 , 甚至是一天的設計 , 看看你會看到同樣的銀河系 。
