probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最難的科學是生物學領域的旅程 , 因為它需要花數億年才能達到最遠的生物學領域 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴各位 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來沒有做過像生物學領域的旅程 , 我認為我們只能做每幾億年的時間 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星際空間會包含所有在宇宙中的任何一個基礎 , 可以成為我們所謂的 「 知識 」 , 如果知識的存在 , 可以成為我們所謂的 「 知識 」 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們不是一個獨特的穩定的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果有空間可以創造出一個開放式的解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他環境 。 所以 , 地球是如此 。 所以 , 地球是如此 , 幾乎是地球 。 所以 , 地球是如此 , 幾乎是地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	這裡有限的因素 , 不是資源 , 因為它們是很有限的 , 因此 , 不資源 , 因為它們是很有限的 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這個宇宙的知識 , 我認為應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著 , 沒有特定知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有特定知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有任何特定知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有特定知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有任何特定知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有特定知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有特定知識 ,
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只剩下幾光年 , 我們就死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁最近寫了一本書 , 關於我們脆弱的各種事物 , 來自天體物理學 , 科學實驗出錯了 , 最重要的是恐怖主義和武器有關 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機會可以存活下來 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他會在會議上談到這場演講 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為這個議題是正確的分類問題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他說 , 我們可以生存下來 , 我們可以生存 , 我們無法存活下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但 , 不管我們如何創造出相關的知識 , 而是在我們是否創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不是絕對的 , 絕大多數的時間都不行 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終結了 , 所有物種和所有文明已經存在的歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	若我們想成為一個特殊的關係 , 我們的文明 , 與物理的基礎有所不同 , 我們的特殊關係和物理定律 , 我們的特殊關係和物理定律的關係 , 我們的能力可以創造出新的解釋 , 新的知識 , 一個特殊的關係 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我現在向大家介紹一個爭議 , 不是因為我想要提出任何特定的解決方案 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 不是因為我想要提出任何特定的解決方案 , 不是因為我想要提出任何特定的解決方案 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但不是正確的物理學家 , 但我不是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 , 但我不是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我不是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 但不是正確的物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我不是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 但不是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 但不是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我不是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我不是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我不是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我不是物理學家 。 根據這個理論 , 它已經太遲了 , 無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們最好的選項 , 就是要預防二氧化碳排放 , 如kyoto建議 , 在經濟活動上 , 最好的選項就是要預防二氧化碳排放 , 例如 , 經濟活動的限制 , 數百億美元或任何理由 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	投票的行動也不是為了避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能已經太晚了 , 在1970年代末期 , 最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 在1970年代 , 最好的科技理論告訴我們 , 工業排放是要將新冰層結合起來 , 讓數十億人死亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	對我來說 , 我不知道為什麼它不是公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	我們不能總是知道 , 當我們知道一個災難的代價時 , 會如何解決它的成本 , 不只是災難的災難 , 還會造成災難的成本 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 , 我們還沒有預防措施 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	嗯 , 我們需要一個穩定的問題 , 不是只是解決問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	一旦我們知道預防措施的預防 , 會發生什麼事 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你一直在鼻子上 , 科學醫學並不會教導你如何避免懲罰 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學科學停止尋求治癒和專注在預防的情況下 , 那麼它就會變得非常少 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	世界正在進行大規模的氣體排放 , 以致力減少氣體排放量 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	應該要把焦點放在高溫度上 , 但有效率、很便宜 , 有些規則 , 像是在空氣中的鏡子 , 把陽光轉化 , 並鼓勵水平的生物 , 來減少溫度 , 不只如此 , 而是有效率地降低溫度 , 並且在高溫度下降低溫度 , 而有些計劃可以降低溫度 , 並且在高溫度下降低溫度 , 而有些計劃可以降低溫度 , 而有些計劃可以降低溫度 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此時此刻 , 這些東西都是fring研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是中央人力來面對這個問題 , 或問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	對於我們無法解決的問題 , 不只希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以 , 拿兩隻石頭 , 帶著兩隻石頭 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	一方面 , 卡路: 「 問題是luble 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一方面 , 「 問題是不可避免的 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	要如何解決貧窮問題 , 如果它被一系列的國家破壞了 , 經濟學家保羅•羅姆提出了一個大膽的想法: 「 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 城市 , 貧窮的規則 , 卻是經濟學家保羅•羅姆斯 。 」
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題 , 政治 。
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅•羅馬斯的主題是 「 保羅爾羅馬 」 的主題:查爾斯特市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	這對我們來說是個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在家裡工作 , 因為他們沒有任何電力在家裡 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我沒有見過這些特別的學生 , 但我遇到像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	讓我們舉個例子 , 綠色店裡的一個例子 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我將tnelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼 , 尼爾森可以取得一百歲的科技 , 如手機 , 但沒有辦法在家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	在一個字中 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	糟糕的規則可以避免一種贏得的解決方案 , 讓人們可以避免一種贏得的解決方案 , 讓人們可以預防愛爾森的新科技 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個非常低的價格下降低了價格 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它不需要提供資源 , 不管是資源 , 不管是資源 , 還不用多餘的資源 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他發現 , 有一種不同的規則 , 規則是商業賺錢的 , 所以他們有一種不同的規則 , 規則規則 , 規則是有可能有一種不同的規則 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這是一種規則 , nelson購買他的手機公司的規則 , 手機公司的規則 , 讓手機公司的規則是手機公司的規則 , nelson購買他的手機公司 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過這些規則如何運作 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試圖改變規則 , 用電力的規則 , 但從商業和消費者中 , 他們想要保存保存的規則 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以 , 他被困擾了規則 , 讓他無法讓他贏得解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	nelson在街道上被困在街道上 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是 , 試著找出我們如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們是否有一些規則 , 來改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說的是 , 如果我們能給予更多的選擇 , 更多的選擇 , 和更多的選擇 , 和更多的國家 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 這兩者之間的反對會很有用 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領袖的選擇 , 像是給領袖的選擇 , 像是給領袖的選擇 , 像是給領袖的選擇 , 像是給領袖的選擇 , 選擇要給領袖的選擇 , 像是給領袖的選擇 , 選擇要給領袖的選擇 , 例如 , 選擇要給領袖的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們想要選擇能夠繼續消費能源的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以 , 如果你只給一個方塊或摩擦 , 你就會有緊張或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到方法來改變規則 , 就能讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	nelson也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到大規模的破壞法則可以讓人們在黑暗中看到 , 在黑暗的照片中 , 在黑暗的照片中 , 在黑暗中 , 看待在黑暗的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別檢查出亞洲
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 就像是黑洞相對它的鄰居 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	你不會很驚訝 , 北韓的規則則會讓人們在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是 , 了解到北韓、文化、價值觀和信仰 , 都能了解到北韓和法律規則的重要性 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離時 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致了非常多樣性的道路 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以我們可以改變我們人類能改變我們所使用的規則 , 更好 , 更好 , 更糟糕 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個區域 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	在海地 , 在海地 , 在海地上網 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 相較於鄰居 , 和鄰居共和國 , 相同的居民有數量的居民 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	兩種國家都與黑人相比 , 如同伊斯蘭國和洛杉磯一樣 , 只有半數的居民是海地或多數的黨派 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地的法則是壞的 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則是壞的 , 因為政府太強大、壓迫 , 在北韓 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想要創造環境有好的規則 , 我們就不能只是淚下 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們必須找到方法來建構 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國顯然地展示了兩種潛力和規則的挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	在這個圖表中 , 中國是世界上最高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先前的科技 , 像是鋼、印刷、印刷、槍枝 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用 , 至少 , 在那段期間 , 有效的規則 , 能鼓勵傳播這些想法的傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快的採取規則 , 慢慢下來 , 除非世界各地的規則 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 在其他國家 , 中國人都從這些進步開始發展新的規則 , 中國人從這些進步開始發展新的規則 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入保持保持穩定 , 讓世界各地有著穩定的位置 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	中國的平均收入是美國的平均收入 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到 , 大約有三分之三 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在1970年代末期發生了改變 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國長大 , 中國開始很快地使用美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你回到地圖上 , 你就能得到一個線索 , 來到中國的大規模改變規則 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國的最亮點 , 你可以看到在上面的邊緣 , 這裡是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是個小小的中國規則 , 在20世紀中 , 由英國的政府規則 , 由英國而來 , 由英國而來 , 大自然的規則則是如此 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是個地方數百萬人可以從馬地開始工作 , 像是賣衣、玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 要加入越來越多的進步 , 增加的速度會快速成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是模型 , 當他們決定要搬到市場模式時 , 他們決定要移動所有的大陸 , 到市場模式 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但 , 針對對待他人的重要性 , 來決定對他人的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與市場規則相反 , 沒有任何人想要選擇在中國 , 通過創造一些特殊的區塊 , 可以做到 , 例如 , 英國所做的事:讓機會和市場規則交易 , 讓大家能夠去工作 , 以某種特殊的區塊 , 為他們創造一些特殊區塊 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們創造了四個特殊的經濟區塊 , 城市長大 , 城市長大 , 都市長大 , 城市長大迅速 , 城市長大 , 和城市長大 , 都市長大 , 都市長大 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港的一個城市叫做nzhen 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在這個城市裡 , 有一個塔iphone , 裡面有許多人的工廠 , 他們用勞動力 , 讓iphone和中國人一起工作 , 他們從中國人搬到華盛頓 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特殊區塊裡 , 有14個海岸線 , 在那裡 , 人們可以選擇 , 最終會成功 , 這些地方的人們可以選擇 , 最終會成功 , 這些地方的人們可以選擇 , 最終會成功 , 讓人們可以選擇 , 最終會成功 , 讓人們可以選擇 , 最終會成功 , 讓人們可以選擇 , 最終會成功 , 讓人們可以選擇 , 最終會成功 , 這些地方的人們可以選擇 , 最終會成功 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	展示成功的成功 , 讓整個經濟的成功變得更加密切 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了我們幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保存選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:正確的規模 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變規則的規則 , 你就能做到 , 但村子的村子太小了 , 你能做到 , 但村子有數百萬人都在良好的規則中工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變規則 , 你不能給一些人有機會來回顧 , 看看事情如何轉變 , 讓其他人有機會回顧 , 看看如何轉移 , 讓其他人有機會回顧 , 看看如何轉移 , 讓其他人有機會回顧 , 看看事情如何轉移 , 讓其他人有機會回顧 , 看看
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你一個機會創造新的規則 , 人們可以選擇的新地方 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	他們很大 , 足以讓所有受益的利益 , 只要數百萬人在好的規則中 , 才能得到所有利益 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	因此 , 建議是我們所謂的 「 大城市 」 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一系列的規則開始 , 所有規則都需要吸引我們要建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 建造出基礎建設的電力系統、道路、機場、港口、機場 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 誰會來僱用那些搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 讓孩子們得到教育 , 給他們的孩子 , 取得他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這些圖表 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以建造 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴展這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以再一次地做一次 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它運作 , 我們需要好的規則 , 我們已經討論了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些都是被捕捉到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要選擇給人們 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這實在是建造城市在未被建設的城市 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未被居住的領土 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以住在新查爾斯 , 但沒有人被迫活下去 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是選擇領導者 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成目標 , 我們想要領導人的選擇 , 我們需要讓大家能參與國際關係 , 例如 , 中國和英國共同合作 , 建立第一個小規模的市場模型 , 並在中國和英國合作建立起第一步 , 讓它能在中國和英國之間合作 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國很不幸地 , 在過去一世紀中 , 沒有任何援助計畫 , 才能減少世界貧窮 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們允許這種合作夥伴 , 我們就能得到這些類型的益處在世界各地 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 該國有責任的責任 , 來自一個國家的另一種國家 , 以某種程度的責任 , 來控制一個國家的責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我說 , 你們有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是 , 但很重要的是 , 當我們開始思考這些東西時 , 可以把我們帶回來的情緒 , 可以讓我們回頭 , 可以把我們的能力帶回去 , 去探索新的想法 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不是殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	關於殖民主義的差異 , 對於殖民主義的影響 , 和我們對殖民主義的差異很糟糕 , 其實我們對於殖民主義有所不同 , 卻在一些我們援助的過程中很糟糕 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是所有選擇 , 包括領導者 , 和那些住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是要避免和接觸 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何在練習中進行練習 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	我們來找一個特定領袖 , 拉克斯特洛 , 他是古巴的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	他必須有機會為中國做這件事 , 但他沒有一個香港在土地上 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 在南方 , 有一個非常特殊的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	這裡有一塊土地 , 一塊土地大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大小 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯特在加拿大 , 說: 「 看 , 黃金會有一個可怕的問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不加拿大 , 加拿大 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立一個特別的管理區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新的城市被建造出來 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人來到這裡 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	咱們來看看一個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	一些我的公民也會搬進城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會繼續回來 , 但這會將現代經濟和現代經濟和現代經濟和現代經濟和現代化經濟和現代經濟體現代化 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 其他這種模式在哪裡呢 ?

many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	其中許多人都可以選擇成為一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	規則是改變規則的規則
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方式 , 讓人們在空氣中 , 沒有武力 , 並且讓人們選出新的規則 , 讓人們不用煤炭 , 並且讓大家在空氣中 , 沒有煤炭 , 並且讓人們在空氣中無法產生新的規則 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也很清楚的承諾 , 只要他們能做得更清楚的承諾 , 只要他們能做得更好的承諾 , 就能做出更可信的承諾 , 在一個新的城市中 , 他們能更清楚的承諾 , 在他們能做出更可信的承諾中 , 在一個新的城市中 , 他們能更清楚地承諾 , 以便能更保守的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	或許甚至有些排列方式有點像是退休金帳戶 , 另一半的國會負責任意 。

you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用在土地上的錢 , 比如警察、法庭、學校系統 , 以及健康照護系統 , 讓它變得更有吸引力 , 讓土地更有吸引力 , 讓土地更有吸引力 , 讓土地更有吸引力 。

let me conclude with this picture .	讓我結論這張照片 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	儘管如此 , 有許多人在地球上 , 是因為這些想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以分享點子 , 和其他人分享點子 , 當他們發現他們 , 他們和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不像稀有的物體 , 分享的意思是 , 我們每一步都比較少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享點子時 , 我們都能得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們想到這些想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:規則 , 我們有不同的規則:規則 , 我們有不同的規則:規則我們如何互動彼此互動的方式 ; 規則 , 例如 , 我們有一個稅制系統 , 來協助一個研究大學 , 來提供一些知識免費的規則 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	我們有一套系統 , 在那裡 , 人們可以把土地放在政府辦公室裡 , 讓人們可以被放到政府辦公室 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	若我們能繼續進步 , 讓世界變得更好 , 像尼爾森和他的朋友不需要研究任何在街道上的規則 。 謝謝你 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因學家先生多元的基因學家先生多樣性 , 他的基因組已經發現了 , 遠遠超過了數百萬個基因組 , 探討了他的團隊發現了它 , 以致於地球的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物學 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	在dna和海面上 , dna和海平面上升 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	一開始 , 我被問過幾個人關於辯論的辯論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我知道樂觀主義者很幸運地悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我們要從讀基因編碼到第一階段 , 開始寫程式碼 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅十年前 , 我們發表了第一序列出版的第一個序列 , 叫做 「 流感流感 」 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這是從13年來的基因組計畫 , 從13年到4個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以做同樣的基因組計畫 , 花了兩到八個小時 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	在過去十年間 , 大量的基因組已被加入:大部分人類的基因組 , 包括人類基因組 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	在這個世紀末期的基因組序列中 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組序列 , 大約十年前 , 已經有三到五個基因組序列 , 大約十年前 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛剛從gordon和bettymoore基金會找到了這個年來序列 , 一個來自環境器官體系的三十個基因組 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 到底在哪裡 , 我們幾乎無法在這個星球上找到什麼 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大多數人並不了解它 , 因為它們是無形的 , 但微生物的數量 , 只有一半的地球生物物質 , 所有動物只佔了地球生物數量的三分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	或許是牛津人並不常常做的事 , 但如果你把海水帶到海水裡 , 每一千萬個細菌和一百萬個細菌 , 就會有一百萬個細菌 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	超過5000種微生物物種已經被分類了 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	然後我們開始了二百英里的海盜獵物 , 嘗試樣本海洋地圖 , 試圖將海洋景象放大海洋地圖 , 試著樣本海洋地位 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們開始在加勒比海海岸 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的 , 我們在一艘船上做這件作品 , 讓年輕人去探索科學 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們把海水放進實驗室裡 , 把它們的dna放回我們的實驗室 , 在不同的小型生物體內 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們的實驗室 , 每24小時 , 我們就能收集不同的尺寸 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	這樣做 , 我們做了一些很棒的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 認為我們眼睛中的視覺色素 , 只有一個或兩個有機體在環境中有著相同的顏色 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有物種都在海洋的溫暖區域中 , 其能量和溝通的力量和溝通 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬個新的基因 , 和五萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在已經把這個空氣放到空氣中 , 由土地基金會所做的 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量了多少病毒和細菌 , 每天都有呼吸 , 尤其是在飛機或閉上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們收集了一些簡單的應用程式 , 我們收集了數十億微生物 , 僅僅是紐約市的一棟大樓 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於這個階段的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	僅僅在資料集中 , 我們在海洋中看到了多樣性的樣本 , 大約在200英里外 , 我們發現幾乎每兩百英里 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	在不同溫度上 , 不同的溫度會降低 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 由溫度紅色的溫度降低 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是紅色的溫暖藍色 , 我們發現有非常大的差異在溫度紅色的溫度下 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是紅色的溫暖藍色 。 我們發現在溫暖和水樣本中有很大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另外一件令人驚訝的是 , 我們可以預測它們的微小組合 , 可以預測根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些從區域到區域的區域 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不令人驚訝的是 , 在深海中 , 最藍光的區域是藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當那裡有許多綠光時 , 它們會看到很多綠色的光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但他們甚至更有可能在極端中看到紫外線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了嘗試 , 了解我們的基因資料 , 我們組合所有資料 , 包括我們所有的資料 , 包括我們所有的資料 , 包括我們所有的資料 , 包括我們所有的資料 , 包括我們所有的資料 , 包含了超過一半的基因資料 , 包含了我們全部的基因資料 , 包含了我們全部的基因資料 , 包含了29萬個基因資料 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試圖把這些發現新的成員 , 發現新的家庭 , 或我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但每一種新的家庭 , 我們都能在環境中加入一些新的家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們在這個星球上最早期的階段發現基本的基因、組成和生命 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們觀察所謂的 「 進化樹 」 , 我們就在右手邊的角落 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	大約29萬個基因組中 , 我們只有2億個基因組 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物聚集在一起 , 我們可能有超過三萬個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為這些基因不僅僅是演化的設計演化 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在基因組合中 , 這種基因組合的概念 , 不是基因組合 , 而是不同的基因組合 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna組成dna組成dna序列的能力 , 在過去十年或兩年間 , 基因組成dna序列非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們第一次想到合成基因組 , 從1995年開始 , 生殖器官的第二個基因組開始 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 說: 「 我心我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一個微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	hemophilus有1800個基因
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 ,
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始做轉變的突破 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	翻譯只是小小的dna在基因編碼中被遺傳密碼 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們在基因中分裂 , 它們會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 把所有基因的基因組成 , 我們稱之為 「 不良基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但結果發現 , 環境非常重要 , 你只能定義一個基本或不健康的基因 , 只能定義一個基本或不健康的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智慧方法 , 與基因組約13個相關的基因組合作 , 我們試著用更直接的智慧方法 , 來找出他們共有的基因組 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們發現 , 只有173種基因共通 , 只有173種基因通通 , 只有173種基因通通 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一顆細胞 , 它就擴大了 , 只要我們在310歲時就發現了 , 它就擴大了 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 根據你的觀點來看 , 也許300到400個基因組 , 依賴你的觀點 , 或許300到400個基因組 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	唯一能證明這些想法的方法就是建立一個人造的染色體 , 並且我們必須在基礎的做法上做這種事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現合成精確的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆•史密斯 , 和我的同事 , 開發了一個令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能合成5 , 000個鹼基酸 , 讓我們能合成5 , 000個鹼基酸 , 讓我們能合成5 , 000個鹼基對抗 , 讓我們能合成5 , 000個鹼基對抗 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一項非常令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把病毒粒子轉換成dna時 , dna會開始驅動這些病毒粒子 , 然後殺害細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒的病毒在一年前被做過 , 但只有一個小兒麻痺症病毒 , 只有十分之一 , 才有三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的漫畫 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這種軟體現在正在建立自己的硬體 , 這也是我們和生物學有關的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上開始評估這個區域 , 我最近在參議院委員會委員會議員 , 特別委員會在委員會議員 , 委員會委員會議員 , 委員會委員會議員 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要讓現實發生在心裡 , 和人們的想像力是很重要的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何病毒都是由基因組組成的 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上會想到伊波拉或小波拉或小東西 , 但dna從這個機體中沒有感染 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使某人製造了小型的基因組 , dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正的安全部門是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯盟 , 在那裡 , 美國和前蘇聯盟 , 做了很多努力 , 來創造生物戰事 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這研究真的被關閉 , 應該要讓設計師病毒在未來更有限 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞生物在兩年內就有可能了 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能是可能在十年內 , 可能性細胞 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	我們現在已經做了幾十種不同的建構 , 因為我們可以把這些人工染色體和基因放進這個人工染色體 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你如何把所有其他人都放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一堆積極的結合系統 , 將它們變成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從機體中產生的 , 可以將三百萬輻射的輻射射殺 , 不被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它的基因組在於24小時後的基因組合成 , 之後它的染色體就會被釋放出來 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這個生物在地球上存在 , 可能在地球上 , 甚至存在於我們的旅行中 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一張玻璃碎片 , 大約有50萬種輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和破裂 , 當微生物坐在底部時 , 會變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡有一張照片發生了什麼事:這張圖表顯示了基因組 , 一百七十萬種輻射 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體的染色體是完全分裂的 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這是同一個dna自動重新組裝24小時後 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真正令人震驚的是這些生物可以做到 , 我們可能有千萬種不同的物種 , 能夠做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合成之後 , 第一個步驟只是移植到細胞中 , 不是基因組 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅僅是了解生物學的基礎 , 還能帶來巨大的潛力 , 不只是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 以及社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	舉例來說 , 來自於二氧化碳的二氧化碳 , 來自於環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道很多不同的路徑 , 數以千計的生物 , 可以捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 用碳從大氣中抽取 , 用碳從大氣層轉換成生物聚合物 , 或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一個有機體 , 來自碳的氧氣 , 和氧氣和氧氣有關 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	同時 , 有許多途徑可以用來製造出甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	由於大量的農場 , 在挪威的過程中 , 將甲烷從氣體中 , 變成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短期內 , 我認為 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 可以創造出一百萬個不同的染色體 , 可以設計一個機器人 , 來製造出一百萬個不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 所有生物學 , 都可以透過螢幕來表演 , 不論你在螢幕上 , 或化學產品 , 或化學產品 , 或化學產品 , 或化學產品 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	為了了解這些基因的角色 , 要了解這些基因的角色 , 將會是非常好的 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們正在嘗試修改光合作用光合作用光合作來產生氫氣直接從陽光開始 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用氧氣產生氧氣 , 我們有氧氣濃度的氫氣 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也結合了細胞 , 製造出乙醇 , 製造乙醇的酵素 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	藥物生產已經在大型實驗室使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	在環境裡的化學 , 比我們最佳化學家所製造出的化學還要複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的源源 , 希望能是食物的源源 , 希望能是食物的源源 , 希望能成為食物的源源 , 希望能成為食物的源源 , 希望能成為食物的源源 , 希望能成為食物的源源 , 希望能成為食物的源源 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究結合 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們從1999年開始實驗開始進行實驗 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物學評估 , 來決定我們是否應該嘗試製造一個人工物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要宗教都參與這個 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為宗教領袖們使用他們的文字 , 來做這些實驗 , 為我們所做的事 。 唯一的終結是生物戰場的重要性 。 唯一的終點是生物戰鬥爭取 。 唯一的終點是生物戰場的真相 。 最後的結果是 , 所有宗教領袖都用他們的雕塑 , 來做這些實驗 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , sloan基金會已經資助了一系列的研究 , 找出風險和對社會的風險和益處 , 和對社會有益處的規則 , 以及這些科學團隊的規則 , 如我自己應該在這個區域進行的 , 我們試圖為我們做好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了對恐怖生物恐怖主義的威脅 , 它們非常簡單的問題 , 我們可以設計東西來製造乾淨能源 , 也許革命化開發中國家能做什麼 , 以及提供各種簡單的處理方式 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimbardo說幸福和成功 , 是我們過去和未來的一部分 。 他建議我們把我們推向過去、現在和未來的一步 , 來改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦 , 企業 , 快樂 , 心智 , 心理學 , 科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo預設了一個健康 。

life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑的 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 再來 , 反思 , 專注和未來的焦點和焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	受歡迎的熱情 , 使得他們很有熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少年女生的性愛滋病 , 直到婚姻 , 很感謝你喬治 , 每年有60% , 一直到婚姻中 , 一直到婚姻 。

now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們嘗試四歲孩子 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	牠們可以有兩隻棉花糖 。 但是如果等到實驗員回來後 , 他們就可以有兩隻 。

what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子在誘惑時會發生什麼事 。

they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒了誘惑 , 之後他們會退休 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特•米迪爾 , 我在史丹佛大學的同事 , 在史丹佛大學的同事 , 花了14年的時間 , 試圖找出不同關於這些孩子的同事 。

time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	觀點是 , 人類體驗的研究 , 或時間分裂 , 或時間分裂 , 或時間分裂 。

and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 他們會變得偏見 , 因為你學會會被偏見 , 因為你學會會被偏見 。
what determines any decision you make ?	決定你做出什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做出一個決定 , 你要做一個決定 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對於某些人來說 , 其他人正在做的事 , 以及你所感受到的是什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而這些人 , 當他們做出決策時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現代 」 , 因為他們的焦點就是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現況是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是說: 「 我在過去所經歷過的情況是什麼樣子 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	他們的決策是基於過去記憶的 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會稱這些人為 「 過去原始 」 , 因為他們焦點在哪裡 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是現在 , 而是未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是在預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱之為 「 未來原理 」 , 他們的焦點就是在未來的方向 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想要辯論 , 思考的矛盾是 , 每一件事都能影響你所做的決定 , 你完全無法理解 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	意思是 , 你有這種偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 , 其中有兩種方式 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式來回應過去 , 兩種方式是未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面或負面上 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以被控制 , 如你所知 , 專注於生命的喜悅 , 不論你生命的喜悅 , 或不論你生命的喜悅 , 或真實主義者並不重要 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以成為未來的目標 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你能成為超越未來的生命:名字 , 生命是從死亡開始的 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出心理能力 , 轉變時間觀點 , 轉換時間的觀點 , 就是你必須學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最樂觀的時刻是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度對未來有高度 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	現代主義的演說 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和真實主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最樂觀的形象就是你從過去的直覺到你的家人、身分和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來的渴望得到新的挑戰 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現場表達的能量是能量 , 探索自己、人、人、人、感覺 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	每次觀點都比較負面 , 比正面更負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來犧牲成功的原因是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲了個人的產業 。 他們犧牲了個人的產業 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲睡眠 , 所以它會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們活著工作、成就及控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我肯定和一些tedstersterstersterstersterstersterstersterstersters
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 我是南布朗克斯區的一個貧窮的孩子 , 一個貧窮的孩子 , 在南布朗克斯區的一個貧窮的孩子 , 當時是南布朗克斯區的貧窮孩子 , 當時是南布朗克斯區的貧窮孩子 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我是一位有史以來最棒的人 , 他們做了這些犧牲 , 因為老師們介入 , 並且讓我未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那棉花糖 , 因為如果你等待你會得到兩隻 , 直到我學到平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我已經加上了專注 , 反而我比以前更有生產力 , 我更有生產力 , 我比以前更有生產力 , 我更有生產力 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們正在應用在許多世界問題上:改變了家庭衝突和保育率 , 改善家庭衝突 , 如同時間比喻 , 增加了五百分之一 , 改善了永續性和保育率 , 改善了永續和保育 , 改善了家庭衝突 , 例如 , 修復家庭衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以 , 最後 , 我想說的是:許多生活的謎題 , 可以透過理解你的時間觀點和其他人的方式來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果是很明顯的 。

and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現甲烷是土地 , 甲烷是土地的水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣層中 , 這樣會看到 , 這種情況發生了許多奇怪的可能性 。 你能有數百公里的海水 , 可以看見這些雲朵 , 可以有數百公里的空氣 , 來預防任何太陽光從水面上升起 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是攝氏350度的溫度 。

and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在地球上 , 它能形成河流和洞穴 , 它可以創造峽谷 , 它可以創造峽谷 , 它可以創造峽谷 , 它可以創造峽谷 , 它可以創造峽谷 , 它能形成河流和洞穴 。

but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到六個月後 , 我們進入軌道 , 直到六個月後 , 我們就開始了 , 直到六個月之後 , 我們就被稱為 「 太空總署 」 的調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	由於太陽系的大氣層 , 土衛六的太陽系中有一半小時 , 將它送到大氣層 , 一半小時以來 , 將它送到大氣層 。

and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 它是一個巨大的探索一個星球 , 來了解一個行星系統 , 對於人類歷史而言 , 人類已經不可思議了 。

and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意我們發現泰坦是個很奇妙的星球 , 但奇怪地理相反 , 地球本身 , 很奇怪地理相反 , 地球本身 , 和豐富的地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到英國的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的一座大小的土地上 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 。

but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在南極 , 我們看到的南極地區 , 發現了這個系統 , 我們在南極看到南極 , 我們在南極看到南極 , 我們發現了這個系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組合 。

moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個區域 , 整個區域 , 南極區域 , 整個區域 , 南極區域 , 整個區域 , 溫度是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這很奇怪 , 地球上的北極圈是熱帶的 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們再加入太空時 , 我們發現從這些碎片中 , 冰粒會擴散到太空中 , 數百英里外 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張圖片放進太空中 , 我們看到這些噴射的光量很大 , 以至於我們看到這些噴射的光量 , 還能在幾千英里外到太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊正在做這些圖像 , 像這樣 , 像這樣 , 像這樣 , 像這樣 , 像這樣 , 想出其他結果來自cassini 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們已經得到了結論 , 這些噴泉可能是從土壤中噴出的液態水 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有有機物質、有機物質、有機物質、有機物質 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能在現代天星探險的環境中 , 或其他的說法 , 可以適應生物的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 不論是陸地或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學的影響 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明 , 基因不曾發生一次 , 但兩倍 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 這意味著 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 這意味著 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 這意味著 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 這意味著 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 它已經發生了幾次 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 這意味著 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 它已經發生了幾次 , 每次都發生在宇宙中 , 大約是十億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	現在 , 地球是唯一的星球 , 我們知道的生命是唯一的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 目前我們所知的唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果在1968年 , 美國太空人在1968年被阿波羅八號太空人拍攝時 , 你就會記得這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	這是第一次 , 地球是從太空中拍攝的 , 它對我們有著巨大的影響 , 以及我們對地球的責任感 , 以及我們對地球的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在加州基金會的第一張照片 , 沒有人眼睛看過的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的一面 , 來自土星的一面 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張圖片中 , 你看到了太陽的圖像 , 你看到了太陽的圖像 , 你看到了太陽的圖像 , 你看到了太陽的圖形 , 你看到了太陽的圖形 , 看到了太陽的圖形 , 你看到的是太陽的圖形 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這張美麗的影像 , 不夠精彩 , 我們能在土星的地圖上看到自己的星球 , 形成一個美麗的圖像 , 和我們自己的星球的影像 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一些深刻的觀點 , 看看我們的小小、藍色星球的地球 , 及其它世界的視覺 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而我們從這個旅程發現的觀點 , 最終的獎勵是我們從這個旅程發現的一半世紀前 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人會在這個短期內 , 發現了無知的道路 , 在這短短的談話中 , 谷歌的globe的地圖 , 用地圖繪製工具 , 讓世界各地的人都使用地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	拉斯坦•卡爾加達:製作地圖對抗災害 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 西卡羅尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾吉斯龐大帝國 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人都需要幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人民和供應給地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 ,
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 它很難相信 , 只有15%的地球被塑造出一個可行的地圖 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國總統發現了世界上最多的問題:沒有細節地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助就來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 40個志工用一個新的軟體來繪製一個新的軟體 , 用一個新的軟體來繪製一萬公里路、三千公里路、三千個醫院、邏輯和信念 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	新軟體他們用了嗎 ? google地圖 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	google地圖 , 每位我們都能在地圖上發現我們所知的地方 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製這些軟體 , 從從路到河流 , 從學校到商店 , 到街坊 , 到街坊 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎得主 , 諾貝爾獎得主 , 大部分發展中國家 , 都要把大量的無人機關注為大量 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 一兆美元的土地 , 沒有在印度的任何地方 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	去年 , 過去一年 , 數千名使用者有數以千計的使用者 , 創造出了數以千計的使用者 , 建立地圖 , 用在一千個使用者中 , 創造出一個完全不可思議的地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	由於熱情使用者的熱情使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在我們來看看一些地圖 , 是由使用者所創造的 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 當我們說話時 , 人們正在繪製世界 , 在這170個國家中 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲的橋樑在塞內加爾的橋樑
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	更接近家 , 盧安 , 盧安 , 盧安 , 盧安 , 加羅拉 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這就是計算幾何學的結果 , 以及機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者 , 一名使用者 , 一名使用者 , 一名使用者 , 一名使用者 , 一名使用者 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們未預期的百分之七十的證據 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴西亞電影makeruliabacha問了為什麼我們只關注暴力的領導者 , 不論是哪個非暴力的領導者 , 會問為什麼我們只關注暴力的領導者 , 不願是巴西亞電影makeruliabacha問為什麼我們只關注暴力的領導者 , 不論是哪裡 ?
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、慈悲、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	茱莉亞:注意到非暴力 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我已經確認了我的人生 , 記錄了伊斯蘭和巴勒斯坦人試圖終止衝突和平的意義 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我旅行到歐洲和美國時 , 一個問題總是出現:那是巴勒斯坦甘地嗎 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼不是巴勒斯坦人使用非暴力抗藥 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我聽到這個問題時 , 通常我剛從中東開始 , 我花了幾年的時間拍攝了幾十位巴勒斯坦人用非暴力來防護他們的土地和水資源 , 用非暴力來防護他們的土地和水資源 , 用非暴力來防護他們的土地和水資源 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者試圖要把大規模的國家非暴力運動結合起來 , 並建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 你們大部分人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	在地面和平面上 , 發生了什麼事 , 和平的抗議性運動已經成功了 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我來談談注意力的力量 , 關於注意力的力量 , 注意力的力量 , 注意力的力量 , 注意力的力量 , 關注的權力 , 以及在西非暴力運動的力量 , 但現在 , 我的案例研究是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 對於巴勒斯坦人來說 , 要開始採取非暴力的行為 , 而是為了我們開始注意到那些已經存在的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明一下這個村莊叫做布德魯斯的村子 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨滅絕 , 因為以色列宣布 , 要建設一個隔離障礙 , 其中一部分會在村落裡建造一個隔離障礙 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 所以他們失去了40%的土地並被周圍 , 所以他們失去了40%的土地並被周圍 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過啟發和平的抗議活動 , 他們發出了一個和平的抗議活動 , 阻止發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你有感覺到地面上看起來是什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦婦女:我們被告知牆會分開巴勒斯坦婦女 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們意識到牆會偷我們的土地 。

fatah , hamas and the popular front !	哈馬斯和普通的前面 !
