julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞•巴基:當我第一次聽到關於布德魯的故事時 , 我很驚訝 , 在2003年 , 國際媒體已經失敗了 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德魯斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 在10個月後 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦之間的協議 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦的國際間隔離他們的土地 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦領土 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	巴勒斯坦的社區在耶路撒冷的抗議 , 布德魯斯林尼亞鄰里 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然在這些故事中感到沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默的後果可能會成長 , 或甚至生存在巴勒斯坦 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭 , 都是一種非常重要的共通點 ; 它們是一種劇場 , 讓觀眾能夠發揮作用 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力犯罪者是唯一的一群人 , 會變得非常困難 , 非暴力的領導者 , 讓這些民眾歧視的機會 , 變成非常困難的 , 非暴力的領導者 , 讓她們的團體變得非常困難 , 非暴力的領導者 , 讓她們的團體變成非常困難的 , 非暴力的領導者 , 讓她們的團體變成非常困難的 , 非暴力的領導者 , 讓她們的團體變成非常困難的 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的注意力可能會出現在房間裡沒有驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	若要讓孩子變得更熱門 , 就會讓孩子變得更熱門 , 讓孩子變得更熱門 , 讓孩子變得更熱門 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	童年心理學家稱之為功能性行為 , 因為孩童的心理學家稱之為功能性行為 , 因為孩童的心理學家稱之為功能性行為 , 因為孩童的心理學家稱之為功能性行為 , 因為孩童的心理學家稱之為功能行為 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以鼓勵或把注意力放在孩子身上 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區的行為和國家都能受到影響 , 依賴國際社群選擇聚焦注意力 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在中東和平的關鍵行為 , 將非暴力行為帶給我們 , 將非暴力的領導者轉換為非暴力的領導者 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在加薩和東耶路撒冷的電影裡 , 我看到了影響 , 甚至記錄電影可以影響到這個轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個村莊 , 叫做瓦拉jeh , 這位非常親近的jeh , 位於布德魯斯的村落裡 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被圍繞著 , 失去了許多土地 , 沒有自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們使用非暴力的兩年來 , 因為沒有人注意力 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們重建了最好的示範 , 並且將最好的示範給約會 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們在電影中看到了布德魯斯的紀錄片 , 感覺到 , 人們會在電影中看到他們所做的事 , 人們會追隨他們所做的事 , 人們會追蹤他們在做的事 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	以色列為索利亞里特 , 有一個新的和平運動 , 叫做索利亞里 , 這代表在伊斯蘭教堂 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這種運動的領導者已經使用布德魯斯 , 作為他們主要的工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導了非暴力的力量 , 開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	華拉jeh和seh和seh和seh的例子 , 讓非暴力轉變成一個功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 強大媒體播放者的力量 , 只要他們開始覆蓋整個週非暴力的暴力事件 , 像是布林、華爾 , 伊斯坦 , 伊斯蘭 , 伊斯坦 , 伊斯蘭 , 伊斯蘭教 , 不暴力的領導者會變得更明顯、有價值觀 , 和他們工作的力量 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的事情是要了解如果我們不把注意力投入這些努力 , 他們就隱形了 , 就像從未發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但 , 首先 , 我先舉手 , 若我們這麼做 , 他們會多次 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們多大 , 他們的影響會成長在巴勒斯坦的衝突中 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力可以終於阻擋這個情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明非暴力工作在像布德魯那樣的地方 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給他們注意力 , 讓他們可以證明它的工作 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•沙克有個很簡單但強大的模型 , 鼓舞人心的領導力 , 包括蘋果、馬丁•路德•金恩 , 和 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德•金恩 , 和德國王 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	商業、企業、商業、企業、企業、領導、銷售、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙斯坦克:偉大的領導者鼓舞行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不如我們假設時 , 會怎麼解釋 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好 , 你要如何解釋當其他人能夠達成這些假設時 , 會怎麼解釋 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果這麼創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	一年 , 一年後 , 他們比所有競爭者更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一台電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像所有人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的顧問 , 同一群體 , 同一群體 , 同一批評論 , 同一個公司 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有不同的東西 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼是馬丁路德•金恩領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一的男人 , 他肯定不是唯一的美國人 , 他也不是唯一的男人 , 他肯定不是唯一的男人 , 他肯定不是唯一的男人 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼 , 萊特兄弟能夠找出控制權力 , 權力飛行的人 , 更好的資金 , 更好的資金 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成權力的飛行員 , 萊特兄弟們打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界的看法 , 甚至深深地改變了我的觀點 , 甚至徹底改變了我的觀點 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 所有偉大的激勵領袖和組織在世界各地 , 不論是蘋果或馬丁路德•金或馬丁•路德•金或馬丁•路德•金或馬丁•路德•金或馬丁•路德•金或馬丁•路德•金或馬丁•路德•金或馬丁•路德•金或馬丁•路德•金或馬丁•路德•金恩
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這完全相反對其他人 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是把這個世界最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圓 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導者能夠鼓舞其他人不存在 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我定義一下很快的詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上的每一個組織 , 都知道他們做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們如何做 , 無論你是否稱它為你所謂的 「 不論你是如何 」 、 「 不論你 」 、 「 職業過程 」 或 「 不管你是如何 」 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但 , 非常少人或組織知道他們為何要這麼做 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	「 為何 」 , 我並不表示 「 為何 」 做利潤 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 。 結果總是會結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	「 為何 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的信念是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為何要有人關心 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們所做的 , 是我們如何溝通的方式 , 從外面來看 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 , 我們從最清楚的事物到最明確的 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵領袖和鼓舞人士 , 不管他們的產業都認為 , 激勵領導者和靈感組織 , 不管他們的產業 , 都認為 , 和激勵的領導者和鼓舞人士 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我使用蘋果 , 因為他們很容易理解 , 每個人都得到它 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果就像每個人一樣 , 可以聽起來像這樣: 「 我們做出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們是美麗的設計 , 簡單使用和使用者友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一個嗎 ? 「 啊 ! 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這是最多的銷售量 , 大部分的銷售量是多數人的 , 大部分的銷售是多數人的 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們是怎麼樣的 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們會說我們是怎麼樣的 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們會說我們是怎麼樣的 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們會說我們是怎樣的 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們會說我們如何做 ,
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律 , 我們有最好的律師 , 最好的律師 , 我們總是為了客戶做事業 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很棒的氣體電池 , 那裡有天空氣 , 那裡有天花板 , 可以買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這是蘋果的溝通方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀的現況 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思考方式 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓我們的產品漂亮設計 , 簡單使用和使用者友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是為了製造很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同嗎 ? 你準備好要買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是反對資訊的信息 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它證明了我們是人們不買你做的事 , 人們會買你做的事 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你做的事 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋為何每個人在這個房間裡都非常舒適地買電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常舒適地買一個來自蘋果的手機 , 或是來自蘋果的手機 , 或來自蘋果電腦的手機 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如同我之前說的 , 蘋果只是電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何東西可以分辨出他們從任何不同的競爭者身上得到的 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都很平等 , 讓所有這些產品都平等 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們嘗試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 高速公路上發出了螢幕電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們被大量化 , 可以製造平面螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	幾年來 , 他們都在製作螢幕螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	迪爾從3個玩家和pda的產品開始 , 他們做了很好的品質產品 , 他們做出很好的品質產品 , 且他們能做出完美的產品 , 且沒有人買了 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像購買一個mp3玩家 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會買一台電腦公司的一台電腦公司 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你做的事 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標並不是要和所有需要你有的人一起工作 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和那些相信你相信的人一起做商業 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	這是最好的部分:沒有我告訴你的 , 是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	它都是在生物學的基礎 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你仔細觀察人類腦部的功能 , 會發現大腦其實被破碎成三個主要元素 , 完全與黃金圓形相符合 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮質是負責我們所有的理性、分析思想和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個區塊會讓我們的大腦負責 , 我們的肢體大腦負責所有我們的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類行為、決策 , 且沒有能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面交流時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、利益、事實和事實 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它只是沒有驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能透過溝通的方式來溝通時 , 我們會直接對大腦控制行為的大腦控制行為 , 然後讓人們可以用我們所說的和做的方式來分辨 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是猜決定從哪裡來的 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你會給某人的事實和細節 , 說: 「 我知道所有的事實和細節 , 都能給別人 , 但那只是感覺不好 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這個詞 , 不是 「 感覺 」 對嗎 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦的一部分 , 控制決策並不控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的辦法就是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不好 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	有時候你會說你是你的心臟 , 或是你會帶著你的心靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭打破你的行為 , 那些不是其他身體控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	它在你的肢體大腦中 , 是控制決策和非語言的部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你會這麼做 , 而人們對你做的事 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的事 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣地 , 目標不僅僅是賣給那些相信你所相信的人 , 目標是要賣給那些你相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不僅僅是僱用一個工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 你知道嗎 , 如果你僱用人們 , 是因為他們能做工作 , 他們會為你的錢做工作 , 但如果你僱用那些相信你相信的人 , 他們會為你的錢做工作 , 但如果你僱用人 , 他們會為你的錢做工作 , 但如果你僱用人 , 他們會為你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	另外還有一個更好的例子 , 比萊特兄弟更好 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大多數人不知道samuelpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到20世紀初期 , 電力飛行的追求力人飛行就像是日子的飛行 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpontlangley , 我們假設 , 要成為成功的成功 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的公司失敗了 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的三樣東西:下降 , 不錯的人 , 壞市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總共有三件事 , 讓我們探究它 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley已經五萬美金 , 用了這台飛機飛行器 。
money was no problem .	錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在smithsonian和smithsmithsmithsmithsonian做了一個很棒的點子 , 他知道所有偉大的思想 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用了最好的心智金錢能找到和市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報追隨他周圍 , 每個人都帶著他走 , 每個人都在努力 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	我們從來沒有聽過samuelpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠 , 在華盛頓俄亥俄州、維爾和威爾堡 , 他們沒有我們認為是成功的基礎 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 他們付出他們的夢想 , 由自行車店而來的 , 沒有錢 ; 和紐約時報的孩子們 , 沒有錢 ; 和他們在街頭的路線上 , 沒有錢 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差異是 , 維爾和沃爾是由一個原因 , 由一個信念所驅動 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這個飛行機器 , 它會改變世界 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要有富裕 , 他想要有名人 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富裕的追求 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟的夢想是用血液、汗水和淚水而來的 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人則是為了付錢而做 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說 , 每次有多少次 , 他們會拿五組零件 , 因為那是多次 , 他們會花五個部分 , 因為那就是他們有多次要拿五組零件 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 1903年12月17日 , 萊兄弟飛行了 , 沒有人會去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們在幾天後就發現了 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明 , 萊恩的憤怒被誤解了 , 他安靜了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是個驚人的發現 , 我會改善你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有很有名的 , 他沒有很有名的 , 他沒有得到名字 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你做的事 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你相信的人呢 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一種稱為法律的法律 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你肯定知道這個文學 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們的第一個2%到50%的人是創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的十三分之一 , 我們的人口是早期的成員 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你的早期大量 , 你的大量和你的晚餐 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	那些人買到手機的原因是 , 因為你不能買到手機 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在各個不同的地方 , 但對創新的概念來說 , 若你想要大規模的成功 , 或大規模的預算 , 你不能直到你達成這個目標 , 直到你達成這個目標 , 直到你達成這個目標 , 就能達到這個目標 , 直到你達成這個目標 , 直到你達成這個目標 , 直到你達成這個目標 , 直到你達成這個目標 , 直到你達成這個目標 , 直到你達成了這個目標 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你對新商業的看法是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你: 「 喔 , 大約10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以試驗超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的人 , 只是 「 得到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們描述它們的方式 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	這就像是腸道一樣的感覺: 「 喔 , 他們只是拿到它 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你在做商業時 , 會如何找到你在做生意之前做的事 , 而不是誰 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 這是這個小小的差距 , 你所看到的 , 最早的大部份不會嘗試 , 直到有人嘗試過它 , 首先 , 這種小小的差距 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期的選民 , 他們很舒適地做出這些決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更舒適地做出這些直覺的決策 , 讓他們相信這個世界 , 而不只是產品的產品 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人是站在六個小時買一台iphone , 當他們第一次出櫃時 , 你只要走進店裡 , 買一台iphone , 只要走進店裡 , 買一台iphone , 只要走進店裡 , 就能買一台iphone 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人是花了四萬美元在平台電視上 , 直到他們第一次出去時 , 即便科技是被送到的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為科技太棒了 , 他們也為自己做 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做的事 , 以及你所做的事 , 會為你所做的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	有人買了iphone在六小時內 , 因為他們所相信的世界 , 以及他們如何希望每個人看到他們:他們是第一個 。

how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你要如何記得你在哪裡停車 ? 你怎麼知道你在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你在哪裡 ? 怎麼知道你在幹嘛 ? 你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 怎麼知道你在正確的方向 , 神經學家neilfgess研究了神經元素 , 和記憶和想像力有關 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾瓦格斯:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們公開車子時 , 我們如何記得我們停車在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這裡有個問題 ,
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著了解他腦中發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們從海馬體開始 , 以yellow為中心 , 這是記憶的記憶 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有傷害 , 像是阿茲海默症 , 你無法記住東西包括你停車在哪裡 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它叫做 「 海馬 」 , 它是 「 海馬 」 的意思 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像其他的大腦一樣 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦有大約一億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元會互相溝通 , 透過傳送一些脈衝 , 或神經元彼此溝通 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩個細胞組成的 , 它們非常密切相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家已經開始了解 , 透過記錄從個人神經元的神經元中 , 或老鼠 , 或老鼠 , 來了解如何運作 , 透過記錄從單個神經元中記錄下來 , 或老鼠 , 或探索環境尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們要想像我們正在記錄從一個神經元的海馬體 , 到這裡的海馬體 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出電力時 , 會有一個紅點和點點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到的是這個神經元知道 , 當這個神經元知道 , 當這個神經元知道時 , 這種神經元就會在環境中找到一個特定的位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它訊號到大腦的訊號 , 傳送一個小電動脈 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以看到神經元的功能是動物的特性 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從不同類的神經元發出 , 我們就會看到不同神經元的不同神經元 , 會發現不同神經元的不同部分 , 如同在這個平方的盒子裡 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們把它們的圖片放到腦部的地圖上 , 說: 「 我現在在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。

well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線非常重要 。

and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果旗幟在一個小型平方環境下方 , 你可以看到 , 如果旗幟在一個小型平方環境下 , 就會出現在一個小平方環境中 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方環境下 , 你就會看到 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方環境下 , 會怎麼樣 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方環境下 , 你就會看到 , 如果旗子在一個小平方環境下 , 會怎麼樣 ?
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	正如你所想的 , 在那個地點的位置 , 你能回到那個地方的位置 , 然後你可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方的位置 , 然後你可以回到那個位置 , 然後你可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你可以回到那個位置 , 然後你可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方的位置 。

so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們把一些遙遠的路徑帶走 , 我們就知道 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 我們會知道 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們能在這個路徑上走路 , 才能整合這條路徑 , 才能整合這條路徑 , 才能整合這條路徑 , 才能整合這條路徑 。

do people have grid cells ?	人們有網幹細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	由於這些特定的神經活動 , 代表網際網路活動 , 每個網格細胞的特定部位都應該改變 , 例如 , 每一條線路徑 , 都應該改變我們是否在六個方向中跑步 , 或跑到六個方向 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放到mri掃描儀中 , 讓他們做一些小影片遊戲 , 就像我給你們看的一樣 , 看看這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	實際上 , 你在人類皮質上看到的是 , 大腦的一部分是大腦的一部分 , 你可以看到在人心皮質上 。
so back to homer .	回到家鄉 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能記得他的車子在距離和方向的距離和方向 , 讓建築物和方向擴展到建築物和邊緣的位置 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這就代表了 , 由神經細胞組成的神經細胞 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從車輛停車場的路徑 , 它會被代表在網格細胞的路上 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都可以讓細胞發出 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回歸到地位的位置 , 在那裡他停車開車的位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個位置的視覺上 , 像是他的車子是否存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被丟棄了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道他在哪裡 , 所以他知道他要去哪裡 , 所以他知道他要去哪裡 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 不幸的是 , 只要我們在整個腦中看到它 , 我們就會看到它在整個腦部的運作 , 我們在整個腦部中看到它 , 我們在整個腦部中看到它 , 我們會看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 ,
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是神經機制 , 代表我們周圍空間的活動 , 可能是神經機制 , 來代表我們周圍的空間 , 可能是神經機制 , 來代表我們周圍的空間 , 可能是神經機制 , 來代表我們周圍的空間 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞開始 , 讓細胞可以從地方細胞開始 , 讓細胞產生出你周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種類型的細胞 , 例如 , 我沒有提到 , 腦部的方向細胞 , 正如你所面臨的一樣 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義觀看的方向 , 你可以想像你在這個婚禮上發生什麼事 , 例如 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個例子 , 一個新的時代在認知神經元中 , 我們開始了解心理過程 , 例如你記得或想像 , 甚至思考一下 , 由數十億個神經元構造出來的大腦 。

imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 全球安全的開放原始碼 , 來自最近的軍事歷史來解釋為什麼安全的未來應該要建造橋樑 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作 , 全球議題 , 公開資源 , 和平 , 政治 , 社交媒體 , 暴力 , 戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史維里德:納多納多是美國最高的員工們對全球安全的看法 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談談開放資源安全 , 因為我們必須在21世紀更好的安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我開始說 , 咱們來回二十世紀 , 來看看二十世紀 , 看看二十世紀 , 看看二十世紀 , 看看二十世紀 , 看看二十世紀 , 看看二十世紀 , 看看二十世紀 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這位是北方 , 法國北方是北方的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在1916年 , 約有70萬人死了 , 大約有2 , 000人死亡 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你在第二次世界大戰時 , 你看到戰爭的戰役 , 三百天 , 兩百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從戰爭的第一次世界大戰結束 , 接著我們進入冷戰 , 伊朗的曲線 , 第二次世界大戰的戰場 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的重點是 , 我們不需要建造橋樑 , 也需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是來自華盛頓特區的一座大樓 , 由伊斯蘭教授 , 和巴爾斯坦所說的 , 關於它如何在歐洲和巴爾斯坦的橋下 , 一路很深入地 , 討論了如何 , 對於歐洲和巴爾斯坦所帶來的影響 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 幾十年來 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 開始看到這些社區開始 , 開始看到這些社區開始 , 開始看到這些社區 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會說 , 開放資源安全是聯合國際網路 , 公共衛生 , 公開資源安全是連結國際、私人的公共空間 , 並且在社交網路上分享 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我來談一下為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們全球公共事 , 都在各式各樣的威脅中 , 以致於全球公共 , 都受到威脅的威脅 , 全球常見會被建立牆壁 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我是很明顯的 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一艘船 , 橫跨印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有甚麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它有保留區的線條 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	要防止海盜來防止海盜 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	piracy是一個非常活躍的威脅 , 在印度海洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	piracy也在馬拉卡的歷史上非常活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它是活躍的在瓜地 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到它 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	這是在全球運輸系統中百分之十的百分之十點 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20個船員 , 500名馬丁爾人 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是全球常見的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉換到不同的海洋 , 網路海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩位年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	那時 , 他們被監禁 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一項信用卡詐欺 , 給他們超過10億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 是全球經濟的一部分 。
two trillion a year .	每年有兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是在英國的gdp 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以這個網路海 , 我們所知道的根本的基礎是激進的基礎 , 完全是徹底的基礎 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	另一件我擔心的事情是威脅會被販賣 , 從阿富汗到美國 , 從阿富汗到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心古柯鹼來自東北地區 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心人口販運 , 和販賣的風險 , 可能 , 我們擔心的是非法武器和販賣的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	交易運行在海中運行 , 但在全球公共的另一部分 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴各位 , 這是一張非常高科技的美國海軍隊員 , 希望能告訴你們 , 這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴各位 , 這是一張非常高科技的美國海軍隊伍軍隊 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這對毒品管道有很大的影響 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它在南美洲的叢林中建造 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們拿了六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個 , 複雜的溝通 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這類販賣 , 包括武器 , 人類 , 武器 , 大規模毀滅的武器 , 是全球共通的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	咱們在阿富汗交談 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一場 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上90%的貧民窟和海洛因 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	我們也看到 , 當然 , 恐怖主義
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這就是蓋達組織的位置 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的緊急擁護 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以恐怖主義的擔憂是全球共同的一部分 , 我們必須解決 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 這是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道20世紀的工具無法運作 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我會說 , 我們不會把安全帶到槍枝的安全之下 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會把安全帶到槍枝的安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要使用軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這麼做時 , 我們必須做得很好 , 很快 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 公開資源安全是國際、私人和網路的聯繫 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子說明這如何運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗 。
they are all holding books .	他們全都包含書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 , 我以為我讀了這位年輕男性和女性 , 二十三十歲的年輕人和女性在阿富汗 。 」
you would be correct .	你是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	85%無法讀到阿富汗的安全力量 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班的教育在時間期間 , 這些男人和女人都學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在書裡 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們正在教導他們閱讀文學 , 與私人部門合作 , 和開發機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教導了超過200 , 000個阿富汗安全力 , 來閱讀和寫字 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你讀和寫在阿富汗 , 你通常會把筆放在你的口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	當這些年輕男性和女性畢業時 , 他們拿著一筆錢 , 把錢帶進口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這裡有50個國家參與這個任務 , 這些發展機構和私人公共和私人合作 , 來處理這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	現在 , 我們也教他們對抗技能 , 當然 , 但我會說 , 開放資源安全的運作方式 , 會使得更久的安全效應 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一個姐姐的船叫做 「 默斯特 」 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這樣一來 , 舒適圈在加勒比海和海岸南美洲各地的營運加勒比海和海岸 , 都在加勒比海和海岸進行治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	一般來說 , 他們會做40萬個病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它不是被軍隊所包容的 , 而是透過軍隊的結合 , 一個人道組織的結合: 「 希望 , 微笑 。 」
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織志願者 。
interagency physicians come out .	醫師們出來了 。
they're all part of this .	它們都是這樣的 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子 , 來看看這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 和他的母親兩天來到眼睛診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被送入時 , 他突然被視著 , 說: 「 mamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamama ,
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽 , 我看到世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	通過四十萬個病人治療 , 這種私人和安全的力量 , 你開始看到創造安全力量的力量 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你看到棒球玩家 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能否選出兩位美國軍士兵在這張照片裡 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是兩位年輕男孩的一部分 。 這是一系列的一部分 , 我們在美國和加勒比海地區 , 都在加勒比海 , 美國和加勒比海 , 美國和加勒比海地區 , 在那裡 , 軍事棒球隊員 , 他們是如此受歡迎的一部分 , 他們將軍事棒球隊員當作戰士 , 其中的一部分是這些年輕男孩的一部分 。 這是一系列的美國和加勒比海 , 美國和加勒比海 , 美國和加勒比海地區 , 全部都在加勒比海 , 美國和加勒比海地區 , 在那裡 , 全部的美國和加勒比海 , 都在加勒比海 , 美國和加勒比海地區 , 都在加勒比海 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它展現了男性和女性的關係 , 關於生活 , 我會爭論 , 為我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這個夥伴關係的另一面是災難 。

in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在所有這些事件中 , 大約30萬人死亡 , 在巴基斯坦的2005年 , 三十萬人死亡 , 大約三十萬人 , 兩萬五千人死亡 , 在巴基斯坦的南極洲地震 , 大約三十萬人死亡 , 在巴基斯坦的地震中 , 大約三十萬人死亡 , 在巴基斯坦的地震 , 海地地震 , 海地地震 , 海地地震 , 甚至在巴基斯坦的地震中 , 大約有三十萬人死亡 , 在巴基斯坦的地震中 , 海地地震 , 海地地震 , 海地地震 , 甚至是地球地震 。

yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	沒錯 , 我們笑 , 但這就是我們如何連結國際、私人和社群 , 來協助創造安全 。

i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	今天 , 我用維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 不是由12個聰明的人組成 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 全都不用維基百科 。

it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	這是個完美的圖像 , 不是我們所有人都能想像的一樣聰明 。

the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的維基百科非常簡單:一個世界 , 每個人都可以自由地分享所有知識的知識 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 透過結合國際、互聯、國際、互聯性、私人的溝通 , 在21世紀 , 我們就能創造出所有安全的安全 。
